 ELIZABETH GASKELL 

 Drop , drop , slow tear ! 
 and bathe those beauteous foot , 
 which bring from heaven 
 the news and Prince of peace . 
 cease not , wet eye , 
 for mercy to entreat : 
 to cry for vengeance 
 Sin doth never cease . 
 in your deep flood 
 Drown all my fault and fear ; 
 nor let his eye 
 see sin , but through my tear . 

 Phineas Fletcher 

 

 

 

 CHAPTER I 

 the Dressmaker 's Apprentice at work 
 

 there be an assize - town in one of the eastern county which be much distinguish by the Tudor sovereign , and , in consequence of their favour and protection , attain a degree of importance that surprise the modern traveller . 

 a hundred year ago its appearance be that of picturesque grandeur . the old house , which be the temporary residence of such of the county - family as content themselves with the gaiety of a provincial town , crowd the street and give they the irregular but noble appearance yet to be see in the city of Belgium . the side of the street have a quaint richness , from the effect of the gable , and the stack of chimney which cut against the blue sky above ; while , if the eye fall lower down , the attention be arrest by all kind of projection in the shape of balcony and oriel ; and it be amusing to see the infinite variety of window that have be cram into the wall long before Mr Pitt 's day of taxation . the street below suffer from all these projection and advanced story above ; they be dark , and ill - paved with large , round , jolt pebble , and with no side - path protect by kerb - stone ; there be no lamp - post for long winter night ; and no regard be pay to the want of the middle class , who neither drive about in coach of their own , nor be carry by their own man in their own sedan into the very hall of their friend . the professional man and their wife , the shopkeeper and their spouse , and all such people , walk about at considerable peril both night and day . the broad unwieldy carriage hem they up against the house in the narrow street . the inhospitable house project their flight of step almost into the carriage - way , force pedestrian again into the danger they have avoid for twenty or thirty pace . then , at night , the only light be derive from the glare , flare oil - lamp hang above the door of the more aristocratic mansion ; just allow space for the passer - by to become visible , before they again disappear into the darkness , where it be no uncommon thing for robber to be in wait for their prey . 

 the tradition of those bygone time , even to the small social particular , enable one to understand more clearly the circumstance which contribute to the formation of character . the daily life into which people be bear , and into which they be absorb before they be well aware , form chain which only one in a hundred have moral strength enough to despise , and to break when the right time come when an inward necessity for independent individual action arise , which be superior to all outward conventionality . therefore it be well to know what be the chain of daily domestic habit which be the natural lead - string of our forefather before they learn to go alone . 

 the picturesqueness of those ancient street have depart now . the Astleys , the Dunstans , the Waverhams name of power in that district go up duly to London in the season , and have sell their residence in the county - town fifty year ago , or more . and when the county - town lose its attraction for the Astleys , the Dunstans , the Waverhams , how could it be suppose that the Domvilles , the bexton , and the wilde would continue to go and winter there in their second - rate house , and with their increase expenditure ? so the grand old house stand empty awhile ; and then speculator venture to purchase , and to turn the deserted mansion into many small dwelling , fit for professional man , or even   bend your ear lower , lest the shade of Marmaduke , first Baron Waverham , hear   into shop ! 

 even that be not so very bad , compare with the next innovation on the old glory . the shopkeeper find out that the once fashionable street be dark , and that the dingy light do not show off their good to advantage ; the surgeon could not see to draw his patient 's tooth ; the lawyer have to ring for candle an hour early than he be accustom to do when live in a more plebeian street . in short , by mutual consent , the whole front of one side of the street be pull down , and rebuild in the flat , mean , unrelieved style of George the Third . the body of the house be too solidly grand to submit to alteration ; so people be occasionally surprised , after pass through a commonplace - look shop , to find themselves at the foot of a grand carve oaken staircase , light by a window of stain glass , story all over with armorial bearing . 

 up such a stair past such a window   through which the moonlight fall on she with a glory of many colour   Ruth Hilton pass wearily one January night , now many year ago . I call it night ; but , strictly speak , it be morning . two o'clock in the morning chime forth the old bell of St Saviour 's . and yet more than a dozen girl still sit in the room into which Ruth enter , stitch away as if for very life , not dare to gape , or show any outward manifestation of sleepiness . they only sigh a little when Ruth tell Mrs Mason the hour of the night , as the result of her errand ; for they know that , stay up as late as they might , the work - hour of the next day must begin at eight , and their young limb be very weary . 

 Mrs Mason work away as hard as any of they ; but she be old and tough ; and , besides , the gain be her . but even she perceive that some rest be need . " young lady ! there will be an interval allow of half an hour . ring the bell , Miss Sutton . Martha shall bring you up some bread and cheese and beer . you will be so good as to eat it stand away from the dress and to have your hand wash ready for work when I return . in half an hour , " say she once more , very distinctly ; and then she leave the room . 

 it be curious to watch the young girl as they instantaneously avail themselves of Mrs Mason 's absence . one fat , particularly heavy - look damsel lay her head on her fold arm and be asleep in a moment ; refuse to be waken for her share in the frugal supper , but spring up with a frightened look at the sound of Mrs Mason 's return footstep , even while it be still far off on the echo stair . two or three other huddle over the scanty fireplace , which , with every possible economy of space , and no attempt whatever at anything of grace or ornament , be insert in the slight , flat - look wall , that have be run up by the present owner of the property to portion off this division of the grand old drawing - room of the mansion . some employ the time in eat their bread and cheese , with as measured and incessant a motion of the jaw   and almost as stupidly placid an expression of countenance , as you may see in cow ruminate in the first meadow you happen to pass . 

 some hold up admiringly the beautiful ball - dress in progress , while other examine the effect , back from the object to be criticise in the true artistic manner . other stretch themselves into all sort of posture to relieve the weary muscle ; one or two give vent to all the yawn , cough , and sneeze that have be pen up so long in the presence of Mrs Mason . but Ruth Hilton spring to the large old window , and press against it as a bird press against the bar of its cage . she put back the blind , and gaze into the quiet moonlight night . it be doubly light almost as much so as day for everything be cover with the deep snow which have be fall silently ever since the evening before . the window be in a square recess ; the old strange little pane of glass have be replace by those which give more light . a little distance off , the feathery branch of a larch wave softly to and fro in the scarcely perceptible night - breeze . poor old larch ! the time have be when it have stand in a pleasant lawn , with the tender grass creep caressingly up to its very trunk ; but now the lawn be divide into yard and squalid back premise , and the larch be pen up and gird about with flag - stone . the snow lie thick on its bough , and now and then fall noiselessly down . the old stable have be add to , and alter into a dismal street of mean - looking house , back to back with the ancient mansion . and over all these change from grandeur to squalor , bend down the purple heaven with their unchanging splendour ! 

 Ruth press her hot forehead against the cold glass , and strain her ache eye in gaze out on the lovely sky of a winter 's night . the impulse be strong upon she to snatch up a shawl , and wrap it round her head , to sally forth and enjoy the glory ; and time be when that impulse would have be instantly follow ; but now , Ruth 's eye fill with tear , and she stand quite still , dream of the day that be go . some one touch her shoulder while her thought be far away , remember past January night , which have resemble this , and be yet so different . 

 " Ruth , love , " whisper a girl who have unwillingly distinguish herself by a long hard fit of coughing , " come and have some supper . you do not   know yet how it help one through the night . " 

 " one run one blow of the fresh air would do I more good , " say Ruth . 

 " not such a night as this , " reply the other , shiver at the very thought . 

 " and why not such a night as this , Jenny ? " answer Ruth . " oh ! at home I have many a time run up the lane all the way to the mill , just to see the icicle hang on the great wheel ; and when I be once out , I could hardly find in my heart to come in , even to mother , sit by the fire ; even to mother , " she add , in a low , melancholy tone , which have something of inexpressible sadness in it . " why , Jenny ! " say she , rouse herself , but not before her eye be swim with tear , " own , now , that you never see those dismal , hateful , tumble - down old house there look half so what shall I call they ? almost beautiful as they do now , with that soft , pure , exquisite covering ; and if they be so improved , think of what tree , and grass , and ivy must be on such a night as this . " 

 Jenny could not be persuade into admire the winter 's night , which to she come only as a cold and dismal time , when her cough be more troublesome , and the pain in her side bad than usual . but she put her arm round Ruth 's neck , and stand by she , glad that the orphan apprentice , who be not yet inure to the hardship of a dressmaker 's workroom , should find so much to give her pleasure in such a common occurrence as a frosty night . 

 they remain deep in separate train of thought till Mrs Mason 's step be hear , when each return , supperless but refresh , to her seat . 

 Ruth 's place be the cold and the dark in the room , although she like it the good ; she have instinctively choose it for the sake of the wall opposite to she , on which be a remnant of the beauty of the old drawing - room , which must once have be magnificent , to judge from the fade speciman leave . it be divide into panel of pale sea - green , pick out with white and gold ; and on these panel be paint be throw with the careless , triumphant hand of a master the most lovely wreath of flower , profuse and luxuriant beyond description , and so real - look , that you could almost fancy you smell their fragrance , and hear the south wind go softly rustle in and out among the crimson rose the branch of purple and white lilac the float golden - tressed laburnum bough . besides these , there be stately white lily , sacred to the Virgin hollyhock , fraxinella , monk's - hood , pansy , primrose ; every flower which bloom profusely in charming old - fashioned country garden be there , depict among its graceful foliage , but not in the wild disorder in which I have enumerate they . at the bottom of the panel lie a holly - branch , whose stiff straightness be ornament by a twining drapery of English ivy and mistletoe and winter aconite ; while down either side hang pendant garland of spring and autumn flower ; and , crown all , come gorgeous summer with the sweet musk - rose , and the rich - colour flower of June and July . 

 Surely Monnoyer , or whoever the dead and go artist might be , would have be gratify to know the pleasure his handiwork , even in its wane , have power to give to the heavy heart of a young girl ; for they conjure up vision of other sister - flower that grow , and blossom , and wither away in her early home . 

 Mrs Mason be particularly desirous that her workwoman should exert themselves to - night , for , on the next , the annual hunt - ball be to take place . it be the one gaiety of the town since the assize - ball have be discontinue . many be the dress she have promise should be send home " without fail " the next morning ; she have not let one slip through her finger , for fear , if it do , it might fall into the hand of the rival dressmaker , who have just establish herself in the very same street . 

 she determine to administer a gentle stimulant to the flag spirit , and with a little preliminary cough to attract attention , she begin : 

 " I may as well inform you , young lady , that I have be request this year , as on previous occasion , to allow some of my young people to attend in the ante - chamber of the assembly - room with sandal ribbon , pin , and such little matter , and to be ready to repair any accidental injury to the lady ' dress . I shall send four of the most diligent . " she lay a marked emphasis on the last word , but without much effect ; they be too sleepy to care for any of the pomp and vanity , or , indeed , for any of the comfort of this world , except one sole thing their bed . 

 Mrs Mason be a very worthy woman , but , like many other worthy woman , she have her foible ; and one   very natural to her calling   be to pay an extreme regard to appearance . accordingly , she have already select in her own mind the four girl who be most likely to do credit to the " establishment ; " and these be secretly determine upon , although it be very well to promise the reward to the most diligent . she be really not aware of the falseness of this conduct ; be an adept in that species of sophistry with which people persuade themselves that what they wish to do be right . 

 at last there be no resist the evidence of weariness . they be tell to go to bed ; but even that welcome command be languidly obey . slowly they fold up their work , heavily they move about , until at length all be put away , and they troop up the wide , dark staircase . 

 " oh ! how shall I get through five year of these terrible night ! in that close room ! and in that oppressive stillness ! which let every sound of the thread be hear as it go eternally backwards and forwards , " sob out Ruth , as she throw herself on her bed , without even undress herself . 

 " Nay , Ruth , you know it will not   be always as it have be to - night . we often get to bed by ten o'clock ; and by - and - by you will not   mind the closeness of the room . you be wear out to - night , or you would not have mind the sound of the needle ; I never hear it . come , let I unfasten you , " say Jenny . 

 " what be the use of undressing ? we must be up again and at work in three hour . " 

 " and in those three hour you may get a great deal of rest , if you will but undress yourself and fairly go to bed . come , love . " 

 Jenny 's advice be not resist ; but before Ruth go to sleep , she say : 

 " oh ! I wish I be not so cross and impatient . I do not   think I use to be . " 

 " no , I be sure not . Most new girl get impatient at first ; but it go off , and they do not   care much for anything after awhile . poor child ! she be asleep already , " say Jenny to herself . 

 she could not sleep or rest . the tightness at her side be bad than usual . she almost think she ought to mention it in her letter home ; but then she remember the premium her father have struggle hard to pay , and the large family , young than herself , that have to be care for , and she determine to bear on , and trust that when the warm weather come both the pain and the cough would go away . she would be prudent about herself . 

 what be the matter with Ruth ? she be cry in her sleep as if her heart would break . such agitated slumber could be no rest ; so Jenny waken she . 

 " Ruth ! Ruth ! " 

 " oh , Jenny ! " say Ruth , sit up in bed , and push back the mass of hair that be heat her forehead , " I think I see mamma by the side of the bed , come , as she use to do , to see if I be asleep and comfortable ; and when I try to take hold of she , she go away and leave I alone I do not   know where ; so strange ! " 

 " it be only a dream ; you know you have be talk about she to I , and you be feverish with sit up late . go to sleep again , and I will watch , and waken you if you seem uneasy . " 

 " but you will be so tired . oh , dear ! dear ! " Ruth be asleep again , even while she sigh . 

 Morning come , and though their rest have be short , the girl arise refresh . 

 " Miss Sutton , Miss Jennings , Miss Booth , and Miss Hilton , you will see that you be ready to accompany I to the shire - hall by eight o'clock . " 

 one or two of the girl look astonish , but the majority , have anticipate the selection , and know from experience the unexpresse rule by which it be make , receive it with the sullen indifference which have become their feeling with regard to most event a deaden sense of life , consequent upon their unnatural mode of existence , their sedentary day , and their frequent night of late watching . 

 but to Ruth it be inexplicable . she have yawn , and loitered , and look off at the beautiful panel , and lose herself in thought of home , until she fully expect the reprimand which at any other time she would have be sure to receive , and now , to her surprise , she be single out as one of the most diligent ! 

 much as she long for the delight of see the noble shire - hall the boast of the county and of catch glimpse of the dancer , and hear the band ; much as she long for some variety to the dull , monotonous life she be lead , she could not feel happy to accept a privilege , grant , as she believe , in ignorance of the real state of the case ; so she startle her companion by rise abruptly and go up to Mrs Mason , who be finish a dress which ought to have be send home two hour before : 

 " if you please , Mrs Mason , I be not one of the most diligent ; I be afraid I believe I be not diligent at all . I be very tired ; and I could not help think , and when I think , I can not   attend to my work . " she stop , believe she have sufficiently explain her meaning ; but Mrs Mason would not understand , and do not wish for any further elucidation . 

 " well , my dear , you must learn to think and work too ; or , if you can not   do both , you must leave off thinking . your guardian , you know , expect you to make great progress in your business , and I be sure you will not   disappoint he . " 

 but that be not to the point . Ruth stand still an instant , although Mrs Mason resume her employment in a manner which any one but a " new girl " would have know to be intelligible enough , that she do not wish for any more conversation just then . 

 " but as I be not diligent I ought not to go , ma'am . Miss Wood be far more industrious than I , and many of the other . " 

 " tiresome girl ! " mutter Mrs Mason ; " I have   half a mind to keep she at home for plague I so . " but , look up , she be strike afresh with the remarkable beauty which Ruth possess ; such a credit to the house , with her wave outline of figure , her strike face , with dark eyebrow and dark lash , combine with auburn hair and a fair complexion . no ! diligent or idle , Ruth Hilton must appear to - night . 

 " Miss Hilton , " say Mrs Mason , with stiff dignity , " I be not accustomed   as these young lady can tell you   to have my decision question . what I say , I mean ; and I have my reason . so sit down , if you please , and take care and be ready by eight . not a word more , " as she fancy she see Ruth again about to speak . 

 " Jenny ! you ought to have go , not I , " say Ruth , in no low voice to Miss Wood , as she sit down by she . 

 " Hush ! Ruth . I could not go if I might , because of my cough . I would rather give it up to you than any one , if it be mine to give . and suppose it be , and take the pleasure as my present , and tell I every bit about it when you come home to - night . " 

 " well ! I shall take it in that way , and not as if I have earn it , which I have not . so thank you . you can not   think how I shall enjoy it now . I do work diligently for five minute last night , after I hear of it , I want to go so much . but I could not keep it up . oh , dear ! and I shall really hear a band ! and see the inside of that beautiful shire - hall ! " 

 

 

 CHAPTER II 

 Ruth go to the Shire - Hall 
 

 in due time that evening , Mrs Mason collect " her young lady " for an inspection of their appearance before proceed to the shire - hall . her eager , important , hurried manner of summon they be not unlike that of a hen cluck her chicken together ; and to judge from the close investigation they have to undergo , it might have be think that their part in the evening 's performance be to be far more important than that of temporary ladies'-maid . 

 " be that your good frock , Miss Hilton ? " ask Mrs Mason , in a half - dissatisfied tone , turn Ruth about ; for it be only her Sunday black silk , and be somewhat worn and shabby . 

 " yes , ma'am , " answer Ruth , quietly . 

 " oh ! indeed . then it will do "   still the half - satisfied tone . " dress , young lady , you know , be a very secondary consideration . conduct be everything . still , Miss Hilton , I think you should write and ask your guardian to send you money for another gown . I be sorry I do not think of it before . " 

 " I do not think he would send any if I write , " answer Ruth , in a low voice . " he be angry when I want a shawl , when the cold weather set in . " 

 Mrs Mason give she a little push of dismissal , and Ruth fall into the rank by her friend , Miss Wood . 

 " never mind , Ruthie ; you be pretty than any of they , " say a merry , good - natured girl , whose plainness exclude she from any of the envy of rivalry . 

 " yes ! I know I be pretty , " say Ruth , sadly , " but I be sorry I have no well gown , for this be very shabby . I be ashamed of it myself , and I can see Mrs Mason be twice as much ashamed . I wish I need not go . I do not know we should have to think about our own dress at all , or I should not have wish to go . " 

 " never mind , Ruth , " say Jenny , " you have   be look at now , and Mrs Mason will soon be too busy to think about you and your gown . " 

 " do you hear Ruth Hilton say she know she be pretty ? " whisper one girl to another , so loudly that Ruth catch the word . 

 " I could not help know , " answer she , simply , " for many people have tell I so . " 

 at length these preliminary be over , and they be walk briskly through the frosty air ; the free motion be so inspiriting that Ruth almost dance along , and quite forget all about shabby gown and grumble guardian . the shire - hall be even more striking than she have expect . the side of the staircase be paint with figure that show ghostly in the dim light , for only their face look out of the dark , dingy canvas , with a strange fix stare of expression . 

 the young milliner have to arrange their ware on table in the ante - room , and make all ready before they could venture to peep into the ball - room , where the musician be already tune their instrument , and where one or two char - woman   strange contrast ! with their dirty , loose attire , and their incessant chatter , to the grand echo of the vaulted room   be complete the dusting of bench and chair . 

 they quit the place as Ruth and her companion enter . they have talk lightly and merrily in the ante - room , but now their voice be hush , awe by the old magnificence of the vast apartment . it be so large , that object show dim at the further end , as through a mist . full - length figure of county worthy hang around , in all variety of costume , from the day of Holbein to the present time . the lofty roof be indistinct , for the lamp be not fully light yet ; while through the richly - paint gothic window at one end the moonbeam fall , many - tint , on the floor , and mock with their vividness the struggle of the artificial light to illuminate its little sphere . 

 high above sound the musician , fitfully try some strain of which they be not certain . then they stop play and talk , and their voice sound goblin - like in their dark recess , where candle be carry about in an uncertain wavering manner , remind Ruth of the flickering zigzag motion of the will - o'-the - wisp . 

 suddenly the room spring into the full blaze of light , and Ruth feel less impressed with its appearance , and more willing to obey Mrs Mason 's sharp summon to her wandering flock , than she have be when it be dim and mysterious . they have presently enough to do in render office of assistance to the lady who throng in , and whose voice drown all the muffle sound of the band Ruth have long so much to hear . still , if one pleasure be less , another be great than she have anticipate . 

 " on condition " of such a number of little observance that Ruth think Mrs Mason would never have end enumerate they , they be allow during the dance to stand at a side - door and watch . and what a beautiful sight it be ! float away to that bound music now far away , like garland of fairy , now near , and show as lovely woman , with every ornament of graceful dress the elite of the county dance on , little caring whose eye gaze and be dazzle . outside all be cold , and colourless , and uniform , one coating of snow over all . but inside it be warm , and glowing , and vivid ; flower scent the air , and wreathe the head , and rest on the bosom , as if it be midsummer . bright colour flash on the eye and be go , and succeed by other as lovely in the rapid movement of the dance . smile dimple every face , and low tone of happiness murmur indistinctly through the room in every pause of the music . 

 Ruth do not care to separate the figure that form a joyous and brilliant whole ; it be enough to gaze , and dream of the happy smoothness of the life in which such music , and such profusion of flower , of jewel , elegance of every description , and beauty of all shape and hue , be everyday thing . she do not want to know who the people be ; although to hear a catalogue of name seem to be the great delight of most of her companion . 

 in fact , the enumeration rather disturb she ; and to avoid the shock of too rapid a descent into the commonplace world of Miss Smiths and Mr Thomsons , she return to her post in the ante - room . there she stand think , or dream . she be startle back to actual life by a voice close to she . one of the dancing young lady have meet with a misfortune . her dress , of some gossamer material , have be loop up by nosegay of flower , and one of these have fall off in the dance , leave her gown to trail . to repair this , she have beg her partner to bring she to the room where the assistant should have be . none be there but Ruth . 

 " shall I leave you ? " ask the gentleman . " be my absence necessary ? " 

 " oh , no ! " reply the lady . " a few stitch will set all to right . besides , I dare not enter that room by myself . " so far she speak sweetly and prettily . but now she address Ruth . " make haste . do not   keep I an hour . " and her voice become cold and authoritative . 

 she be very pretty , with long dark ringlet and sparkle black eye . these have strike Ruth in the hasty glance she have take , before she kneel down to her task . she also see that the gentleman be young and elegant . 

 " oh , that lovely galop ! how I long to dance to it ! will it never be do ? what a frightful time you be take ; and I be die to return in time for this galop ! " 

 by way of show a pretty , childlike impatience , she begin to beat time with her foot to the spirited air the band be play . Ruth could not darn the rent in her dress with this continual motion , and she look up to remonstrate . as she throw her head back for this purpose , she catch the eye of the gentleman who be stand by ; it be so expressive of amusement at the air and grace of his pretty partner , that Ruth be infect by the feeling , and have to bend her face down to conceal the smile that mantle there . but not before he have see it , and not before his attention have be thereby draw to consider the kneeling figure , that , habit in black up to the throat , with the noble head bend down to the occupation in which she be engage , form such a contrast to the flippant , bright , artificial girl who sit to be serve with an air as haughty as a queen on her throne . 

 " oh , Mr Bellingham ! I be ashamed to detain you so long . I have no idea any one could have spend so much time over a little tear . no wonder Mrs Mason charge so much for dress - making , if her work - woman be so slow . " 

 it be mean to be witty , but Mr Bellingham look grave . he see the scarlet colour of annoyance flush to that beautiful cheek which be partially present to he . he take a candle from the table , and hold it so that Ruth have more light . she do not look up to thank he , for she feel ashamed that he should have see the smile which she have catch from he . 

 " I be sorry I have be so long , ma'am , " say she , gently , as she finish her work . " I be afraid it might tear out again if I do not do it carefully . " she rise . 

 " I would rather have have it tear than have miss that charming galop , " say the young lady , shake out her dress as a bird shake its plumage . " shall we go , Mr Bellingham ? " look up at he . 

 he be surprised that she give no word or sign of thank to the assistant . he take up a camellia that some one have leave on the table . 

 " allow I , Miss Duncombe , to give this in your name to this young lady , as thank for her dexterous help . " 

 " oh of course , " say she . 

 Ruth receive the flower silently , but with a grave , modest motion of her head . they have go , and she be once more alone . presently , her companion return . 

 " what be the matter with Miss duncombe ? do she come here ? " ask they . 

 " only her lace dress be tear , and I mend it , " answer Ruth , quietly . 

 " do Mr Bellingham come with she ? they say he be go to be married to she ; do he come , Ruth ? " 

 " yes , " say Ruth , and relapse into silence . 

 Mr Bellingham dance on gaily and merrily through the night , and flirt with Miss Duncombe , as he think good . but he look often to the side - door where the milliner 's apprentice stand ; and once he recognise the tall , slight figure , and the rich auburn hair of the girl in black ; and then his eye seek for the camellia . it be there , snowy white in her bosom . and he dance on more gaily than ever . 

 the cold grey dawn be drearily light up the street when Mrs Mason and her company return home . the lamp be extinguish , yet the shutter of the shop and dwelling - house be not open . all sound have an echo unheard by day . one or two houseless beggar sit on doorstep , and , shivering , sleep , with head bow on their knee , or rest against the cold hard support afford by the wall . 

 Ruth feel as if a dream have melt away , and she be once more in the actual world . how long it would be , even in the most favourable chance , before she should again enter the shire - hall ! or hear a band of music ! or even see again those bright , happy people as much without any semblance of care or woe as if they belong to another race of being . have they ever to deny themselves a wish , much less a want ? literally and figuratively , their life seem to wander through flowery pleasure - path . here be cold , bite mid - winter for she , and such as she for those poor beggar almost a season of death ; but to Miss Duncombe and her companion , a happy , merry time , when flower still bloom , and fire crackle , and comfort and luxury be pile around they like fairy gift . what do they know of the meaning of the word , so terrific to the poor ? what be winter to they ? but Ruth fancy that Mr Bellingham look as if he could understand the feeling of those remove from he by circumstance and station . he have draw up the window of his carriage , it be true , with a shudder . 

 Ruth , then , have be watch he . 

 yet she have no idea that any association make her camellia precious to she . she believe it be solely on account of its exquisite beauty that she tend it so carefully . she tell Jenny every particular of its presentation , with open , straight - looking eye , and without the deepening of a shade of colour . 

 " be it not kind of he ? you can not   think how nicely he do it , just when I be a little bit mortified by her ungracious way . " 

 " it be very nice , indeed , " reply Jenny . " such a beautiful flower ! I wish it have some scent . " 

 " I wish it to be exactly as it be ; it be perfect . so pure ! " say Ruth , almost clasp her treasure as she place it in water . " who be Mr Bellingham ? " 

 " he be son to that Mrs Bellingham of the Priory , for whom we make the grey satin pelisse , " answer Jenny , sleepily . 

 " that be before my time , " say Ruth . but there be no answer . Jenny be asleep . 

 it be long before Ruth follow her example . even on a winter day , it be clear morning light that fall upon her face as she smile in her slumber . Jenny would not waken she , but watch her face with admiration ; it be so lovely in its happiness . 

 " she be dream of last night , " think Jenny .

 CHAPTER III 

 Sunday at Mrs Mason 's

but as he be only a somewhat commonplace farmer , I believe we must attribute his calamity to some want in his character of the one quality require to act as keystone to many excellence . while his wife live , all worldly misfortune seem as nothing to he ;  CHAPTER IV 

 Treading in Perilous Places

Ruth think it be too strong a realisation of her hope , and look for an over - clouding at noon ; but the glory endure , and at two o'clock she be in the Leasowes , with a beat heart full of joy , long to stop the hour , which would pass too quickly through the afternoon . 

 they saunter through the fragrant lane , as if their loitering would prolong the time , and check the fiery - footed steed gallop apace towards the close of the happy day . it be past five o'clock before they come to the great mill - wheel , which stand in Sabbath idleness , motionless in a brown mass of shade , and still wet with yesterday 's immersion in the deep transparent water beneath . they clamber the little hill , not yet fully shade by the overarch elm ; and then Ruth check Mr Bellingham , by a slight motion of the hand which lie within his arm , and glance up into his face to see what that face should express as it look on Milham Grange , now lie still and peaceful in its afternoon shadow . it be a house of after - thought ; building material be plentiful in the neighbourhood , and every successive owner have find a necessity for some addition or projection , till it be a picturesque mass of irregularity of broken light and shadow which , as a whole , give a full and complete idea of a " home . " all its gable and nook be blend and hold together by the tender green of the climb rose and young creeper . an old couple be live in the house until it should be let , but they dwelt in the back part , and never use the front door ; so the little bird have grow tame and familiar , and perch upon the window - sill and porch , and on the old stone cistern which catch the water from the roof .

 why art thou so vexed , o my soul : and why art thou so disquiet within I ?

 they stand together at the top of a steep ascent , " the hill " of the hundred . at the summit there be a level space , sixty or seventy yard square , of unenclosed and broken ground , over which the golden bloom of the gorse cast a rich hue , while its delicious scent perfume the fresh and nimble air . on one side of this common , the ground slop down to a clear bright pond , in which be mirror the rough sand - cliff that rise abrupt on the opposite bank ; hundred of marten find a home there , and be now wheel over the transparent water , and dip in their wing in their evening sport . indeed , all sort of bird seem to haunt the lonely pool ; the water - wagtail be scatter around its margin , the linnet perch on the topmost spray of the gorse - bush , and other hide warbler sing their vesper on the uneven ground beyond . on the far side of the green waste , close by the road , and well place for the requirement of horse or their rider who might be weary with the ascent of the hill , there be a public - house , which be more of a farm than an inn . it be a long , low building , rich in dormer - window on the weather side , which be necessary in such an exposed situation , and with odd projection and unlooke - for gable on every side ; there be a deep porch in front , on whose hospitable bench a dozen person might sit and enjoy the balmy air . a noble sycamore grow right before the house , with seat all round it   ' such tent the patriarch love " ; and a nondescript sign hang from a branch on the side next to the road , which , be wisely furnish with an interpretation , be find to mean King Charles in the oak .

Ruth and Mr Bellingham plunge through the broken ground to regain the road near the wayside inn . hand - in - hand , now prick by the far - spread gorse , now ankle - deep in sand ; now press the soft , thick heath , which should make so brave an autumn show ; and now over wild thyme and other fragrant herb , they make their way , with many a merry laugh . once on the road , at the summit , Ruth stand silent , in breathless delight at the view before she . the hill fall suddenly down into the plain , extend for a dozen mile or more . there be a clump of dark Scotch fir close to they , which cut clear against the western sky , and throw back the near level into distance . the plain below they be richly woode , and be tint by the young tender hue of the early summer , for all the tree of the wood have don their leaf except the cautious ash , which here and there give a soft , pleasant greyness to the landscape . far away in the champaign be spire , and tower , and stack of chimney belong to some distant hide farm - house , which be trace downwards through the golden air by the thin column of blue smoke send up from the evening fire . the view be bound by some rise ground in deep purple shadow against the sunset sky . 

 when first they stop , silent with sigh pleasure , the air seem full of pleasant noise ; distant church - bell make harmonious music with the little singing - bird near at hand ; nor be the lowing of the cattle , nor the call of the farm - servant discordant , for the voice seem to be hush by the brood consciousness of the Sabbath . they stand loiter before the house , quietly enjoy the view . the clock in the little inn strike eight , and it sound clear and sharp in the stillness . 

 " can it be so late ? " ask Ruth .

 in North Wales

 CHAPTER VI 

 Troubles Gather About Ruth 
 

 the next day the weather be brave and glorious ; a perfect " bridal of the earth and sky ; " and every one turn out of the inn to enjoy the fresh beauty of nature .  CHAPTER VII 

 the Crisis Watching and Waiting 
 

 Ruth put away every thought of the past or future ; everything that could unfit she for the duty of the present . exceed love supply the place of experience . she never leave the room after the first day ; she force herself to eat , because his service need her strength . she do not indulge in any tear , because the weeping she long for would make she less able to attend upon he . she watch , and wait , and pray : pray with an utter forgetfulness of self , only with a consciousness that God be all - powerful , and that he , whom she love so much , need the aid of the Mighty one .

 CHAPTER VIII 

 Mrs Bellingham " do the Thing handsomely "

 CHAPTER IX 

 the Storm - Spirit subdue

 CHAPTER x 

 A note and the Answer 
 

 at the inn everything be life and bustle . Mr Benson have to wait long in Mrs Morgan 's little parlour before she could come to he , and he keep grow more and more impatient . at last she make her appearance and hear his story . 

 People may talk as they will about the little respect that be pay to virtue , unaccompanie by the outward accident of wealth or station ; but I rather think it will be find that , in the long run , true and simple virtue always have its proportionate reward in the respect and reverence of every one whose esteem be worth have . to be sure , it be not reward after the way of the world as mere worldly possession be , with low obeisance and lip - service ; but all the well and more noble quality in the heart of other make ready and go forth to meet it on its approach , provide only it be pure , simple , and unconscious of its own existence .

 CHAPTER XIII 

 the Dissenting Minister 's Household 
 

 Miss Benson have resume every morsel of the briskness which she have rather lose in the middle of the day ; her foot be on her native stone , and a very rough set they be , and she be near her home and among known people . even Mr Benson speak very cheerfully to Ben , and make many inquiry of he respect people whose name be strange to Ruth . she be cold , and utterly weary . she take Miss Benson 's offer arm , and could hardly drag herself as far as the little quiet street in which Mr Benson 's house be situate . the street be so quiet that their footstep sound like a loud disturbance , and announce their approach as effectually as the " trumpet 's lordly blare " do the coming of Abdallah . a door fly open , and a light passage stand before they . as soon as they have enter , a stout , elderly servant emerge from behind the door , her face radiant with welcome .

 CHAPTER XV 

 Mother and Child

" 

 " I think it be . I never reason why I feel as I do ; I only know that Mr Bradshaw 's give I a present hurt I , instead of make I glad . " 

 " well , but there be another side of the case we have not look at yet we must think of that , too . you know who say , ' do unto other as ye would that they should do unto you ' ? Mr Bradshaw may not have have that in his mind when he desire his wife to send you this ; he may have be self - seeking , and only anxious to gratify his love of patronising that be the bad motive we can give he ; and that would be no excuse for your thinking only of yourself , and return his present . " 

 " but you would not have I pretend to be oblige ? " ask Ruth . 

 " no , I would not . I have often be similarly situate to you , Ruth ; Mr Bradshaw have frequently oppose I on the point on which I feel the warm be the most earnestly convinced . he , no doubt , think I quixotic , and often speak of I , and to I , with great contempt when he be angry . I suppose he have a little fit of penitence afterwards , or perhaps he think he can pay for ungracious speech by a present ; so , formerly , he invariably send I something after these occasion . it be a time , of all other , to feel as you be do now ; but I become convinced it would be right to accept they , give only the very cool thank which I feel . this omission of all show of much gratitude have the good effect the present have much diminish ; but if the gift have lessen , the unjustifiable speech have decrease in still great proportion , and I be sure we respect each other more . take this muslin , Ruth , for the reason I name ; and thank he as your feeling prompt you . overstrained expression of gratitude always seem like an endeavour to place the receiver of these expression in the position of debtor for future favour . but you will not   fall into this error . " 

 Ruth listen to Mr Benson ; but she have not yet fall sufficiently into the tone of his mind to understand he fully . she only feel that he comprehend she well than Miss Benson , who once more try to reconcile she to her present , by call her attention to the length and breadth thereof . 

 " I will do what you wish I , " she say , after a little pause of thoughtfulness . " may we talk of something else ? " 

 Mr Benson see that his sister 's frame of mind be not particularly congenial with Ruth 's , any more than Ruth 's be with Miss Benson 's ; and , put aside all thought of return to the business which have appear to he so important when he come into the room   but which principally related to himself , he remain above an hour in the parlour , interesting they on subject far remove from the present , and leave they at the end of that time soothe and calm . 

 but the present give a new current to Ruth 's idea . her heart be as yet too sore to speak , but her mind be crowd with plan . she ask Sally to buy she   with the money produce by the sale of a ring or two   the coarse linen , the homely dark blue print , and similar material ; on which she set busily to work to make clothe for herself ; and as they be make , she put they on ; and as she put they on , she give a grace to each , which such homely material and simple shaping have never have before . then the fine linen and delicate soft white muslin , which she have choose in preference to more expensive article of dress when Mr Bellingham have give her carte blanche in London , be cut into small garment , most daintily stitch and make ready for the little creature , for whom in its white purity of soul nothing could be too precious . 

 the love which dictate this extreme simplicity and coarseness of attire , be take for stiff , hard economy by Mr Bradshaw , when he deign to observe it . and economy by itself , without any soul or spirit in it to make it live and holy , be a great merit in his eye . indeed , Ruth altogether find favour with he . her quiet manner , subdue by an internal consciousness of a deep cause for sorrow than he be aware of , he interpret into a very proper and become awe of he . he look off from his own prayer to observe how well she attend to hers at chapel ; when he come to any verse in the hymn relate to immortality or a future life , he sing it unusually loud , think he should thus comfort she in her sorrow for her deceased husband . he desire Mrs Bradshaw to pay she every attention she could ; and even once remark , that he think she so respectable a young person that he should not object to she be ask to tea the next time Mr and Miss Benson come . he add , that he think , indeed , Benson have look last Sunday as if he rather hop to get an invitation ; and it be right to encourage the minister , and to show they respect , even though their salary be small . the only thing against this Mrs Denbigh be the circumstance of she have marry too early , and without any provision for a family . though Ruth plead delicacy of health , and decline accompany Mr and Miss Benson on their visit to Mr Bradshaw , she still preserve her place in his esteem ; and Miss Benson have to call a little upon her " talent for fiction " to spare Ruth from the infliction of further present , in make which his love of patronise delighted . 

 the yellow and crimson leaf come float down on the still October air ; November follow , bleak and dreary ; it be more cheerful when the earth put on her beautiful robe of white , which cover up all the grey naked stem , and load the leaf of the holly and evergreen each with its burden of feathery snow . when Ruth sink down to languor and sadness , Miss Benson trot upstairs , and rummage up every article of spare or wear - out clothing , and bring down a variety of strange material , she try to interest Ruth in make they up into garment for the poor . but though Ruth 's finger fly through the work , she still sigh with thought and remembrance . Miss Benson be at first disappoint , and then she be angry . when she hear the low , long sigh , and see the dreamy eye fill with glitter tear , she would say , " what be the matter , Ruth ? " in a half - reproachful tone , for the sight of suffering be painful to she ; she have do all in her power to remedy it ; and , though she acknowledge a cause beyond her reach for Ruth 's deep sorrow , and , in fact , love and respect she all the more for these manifestation of grief , yet at the time they irritate she . then Ruth would snatch up the drop work , and stitch away with droop eye , from which the hot tear fall fast ; and Miss Benson be then angry with herself , yet not at all inclined to agree with Sally when she ask her mistress " why she keep ' mithere ' the poor lass with ask she for ever what be the matter , as if she do not know well enough . " some element of harmony be want some little angel of peace , in love whom all heart and nature should be draw together , and their discord hush . 

 the earth be still " hide her guilty front with innocent snow , " when a little baby be lay by the side of the pale white mother . it be a boy ; beforehand she have wish for a girl , as be less likely to feel the want of a father as be what a mother , bad than widow , could most effectually shelter . but now she do not think or remember this . what it be , she would not have exchange for a wilderness of girl . it be her own , her darling , her individual baby , already , though not an hour old , separate and sole in her heart , strangely fill up its measure with love and peace , and even hope . for here be a new , pure , beautiful , innocent life , which she fondly imagine , in that early passion of maternal love , she could guard from every touch of corrupt sin by ever watchful and most tender care . and her mother have think the same , most probably ; and thousand of other think the same , and pray to God to purify and cleanse their soul , that they may be fit guardian for their little child . oh , how Ruth pray , even while she be yet too weak to speak ; and how she feel the beauty and significance of the word , " our Father ! " 

 she be rouse from this holy abstraction by the sound of Miss Benson 's voice . it be very much as if she have be cry . 

 " look , Ruth ! " it say , softly , " my brother send you these . they be the first snowdrop in the garden . " and she put they on the pillow by Ruth ; the baby lie on the opposite side . 

 " will not   you look at he ? " say Ruth ; " he be so pretty ! " 

 Miss Benson have a strange reluctance to see he . to Ruth , in spite of all that have come and go , she be reconcile nay , more , she be deeply attach ; but over the baby there hang a cloud of shame and disgrace . poor little creature ! her heart be close against it firmly , as she think . but she could not resist Ruth 's low faint voice , nor her plead eye , and she go round to peep at he as he lie in his mother 's arm , as yet his shield and guard . 

 " Sally say he will have black hair , she think , " say Ruth . " his little hand be quite a man 's , already . just feel how firmly he close it ; " and with her own weak finger she open his little red fist , and take Miss Benson 's reluctant hand , place one of her finger in his grasp . that baby - touch call out her love ; the door of her heart be throw open wide for the little infant to go in and take possession . 

 " ah , my darling ! " say Ruth , fall back weak and weary . " if God will but spare you to I , never mother do more than I will . I have do you a grievous wrong but , if I may but live , I will spend my life in serve you ! " 

 " and in serve God ! " say Miss Benson , with tear in her eye . " you must not make he into an idol , or God will , perhaps , punish you through he . " 

 a pang of affright shoot through Ruth 's heart at these word ; have she already sin and make her child into an idol , and be there punishment already in store for she through he ? but then the internal voice whisper that God be " our Father , " and that he know our frame , and know how natural be the first outburst of a mother 's love ; so , although she treasure up the warning , she cease to affright herself for what have already gush forth . 

 " now go to sleep , Ruth , " say Miss Benson , kiss she , and darken the room . but Ruth could not sleep ; if her heavy eye close , she open they again with a start , for sleep seem to be an enemy steal from she the consciousness of be a mother . that one think exclude all remembrance and all anticipation , in those first hour of delight . 

 but soon remembrance and anticipation come . there be the natural want of the person , who alone could take an interest similar in kind , though not in amount , to the mother 's . and sadness grow like a giant in the still watch of the night , when she remember that there would be no father to guide and strengthen the child , and place he in a favourable position for fight the hard " Battle of Life . " she hop and believe that no one would know the sin of his parent , and that that struggle might be spar to he . but a father 's powerful care and mighty guidance would never be his ; and then , in those hour of spiritual purification , come the wonder and the doubt of how far the real father would be the one to whom , with her desire of heaven for her child , whatever might become of herself , she would wish to entrust he . slight speech , tell of a selfish , worldly nature , unnoticed at the time , come back upon her ear , have a new significance . they tell of a low standard , of impatient self - indulgence , of no acknowledgment of thing spiritual and heavenly . even while this examination be force upon she , by the new spirit of maternity that have enter into she , and make her child 's welfare supreme , she hat and reproach herself for the necessity there seem upon she of examine and judge the absent father of her child . and so the compelling presence that have take possession of she weary she into a kind of feverish slumber ; in which she dream that the innocent babe that lie by her side in soft ruddy slumber have start up into man 's growth , and , instead of the pure and noble being whom she have pray to present as her child to " our Father in heaven , " he be a repetition of his father ; and , like he , lure some maiden   who in her dream seem strangely like herself , only more utterly sad and desolate even than she   into sin , and leave she there to even a bad fate than that of suicide . for Ruth believe there be a bad . she dream she see the girl , wandering , lost ; and that she see her son in high place , prosperous but with more than blood on his soul . she see her son drag down by the cling girl into some pit of horror into which she dare not look , but from whence his father 's voice be hear , cry aloud , that in his day and generation he have not remember the word of God , and that now he be " torment in this flame . " then she start in sick terror , and see , by the dim rushlight , Sally , nod in an arm - chair by the fire ; and feel her little soft warm babe , nestle up against her breast , rock by her heart , which yet beat hard from the effect of the evil dream . she dare not go to sleep again , but pray . and every time she pray , she ask with a more complete wisdom , and a more utter and self - forget faith . little child ! thy angel be with God , and draw her nearer and nearer to he , whose face be continually behold by the angel of little child . 

 

 

 CHAPTER XVI 

 Sally Tells of her Sweethearts , 
 and discourse on the Duties of Life 
 

 Sally and Miss Benson take it in turn to sit up , or rather , they take it in turn to nod by the fire ; for if Ruth be awake she lie very still in the moonlight calm of her sick bed . that time resemble a beautiful August evening , such as I have see . the white , snowy rolling mist cover up under its great sheet all tree and meadow , and token of earth ; but it can not rise high enough to shut out the heaven , which on such night seem bend very near , and to be the only real and present object ; and so near , so real and present , do heaven , and eternity , and God seem to Ruth , as she lie encircle her mysterious holy child . 

 one night Sally find out she be not asleep . 

 " I be a rare hand at talk folk to sleep , " say she . " I will try on thee , for thou must get strength by sleep and eat . what must I talk to thee about , I wonder . shall I tell thee a love story or a fairy story , such as I have   tell Master Thurstan many a time and many a time , for all his father set his face again fairy , and call it vain talk ; or shall I tell you the dinner I once cook , when Mr Harding , as be Miss Faith 's sweetheart , come unlooked for , and we would nought in the house but a neck of mutton , out of which I make seven dish , all with a different name ? " 

 " who be Mr Harding ? " ask Ruth . 

 " oh , he be a grand gentleman from Lunnon , as have see Miss Faith , and be strike by her pretty look when she be out on a visit , and come here to ask she to marry he . she say , ' no , she would never leave Master Thurstan , as could never marry ; ' but she pin a deal at after he go away . she keep up afore Master Thurstan , but I seed her fretting , though I never let on that I do , for I think she would soon get over it and be thankful at after she have the strength to do right . however , I have   no business to be talk of Miss Benson 's concern . I will tell you of my own sweetheart and welcome , or I will tell you of the dinner , which be the grand thing I ever do in my life , but I think a Lunnoner should never think country folk know nothing ; and , my word ! I puzzle he with his dinner . I be doubt whether to this day he know whether what he be eat be fish , flesh , or fowl . shall I tell you how I manage ? " 

 but Ruth say she would rather hear about Sally 's sweetheart , much to the disappointment of the latter , who consider the dinner by far the great achievement . 

 " well , you see , I do not   know as I should call they sweetheart ; for except John Rawson , who be shut up in the mad - house the next week , I never have what you may call a downright offer of marriage but once . but I have once ; and so I may say I have a sweetheart . I be begin to be afeard though , for one like to be ax ; that be but civility ; and I remember , after I have turn forty , and afore Jeremiah Dixon have speak , I begin to think John Rawson have perhaps not be so very mad , and that I have do ill to lightly his offer , as a madman 's , if it be to be the only one I be ever to have ; I do not   mean as I would have have he , but I think , if it be to come o'er again , I would speak respectful of he to folk , and say it be only his way to go about on all four , but that he be a sensible man in most thing . however , I would have my laugh , and so have other , at my crazy lover , and it be late now to set he up as a Solomon . however , I think it would be no bad thing to be try again ; but I little think the trial would come when it do . you see , Saturday night be a leisure night in counting - house and such - like place , while it be the busy of all for servant . well ! it be a Saturday night , and I would my baize apron on , and the tail of my bed - gown pin together behind , down on my knee , pipeclaye the kitchen , when a knock come to the back door . ' come in ! ' say I ; but it knock again , as if it be too stately to open the door for itself ; so I get up , rather cross , and open the door ; and there stand Jerry Dixon , Mr Holt 's head clerk ; only he be not head clerk then . so I stand , stop up the door , fancy he want to speak to master ; but he kind of push past I , and tell I summut about the weather   as if I could not see it for myself , he take a chair , and sit down by the oven . ' cool and easy ! ' think I ; mean hisself , not his place , which I know must be pretty hot . well ! it seem no use stand wait for my gentleman to go ; not that he have much to say either ; but he keep twirl his hat round and round , and smooth the nap on't   with the back of his hand . so at last I squat down to my work , and think I , I shall be on my knee all ready if he put up a prayer , for I know he be a Methodee by bringing - up , and have only lately turn to master 's way of thinking ; and they Methodees be terrible hand at unexpected prayer when one least look for them . I can not   say I like their way of take one by surprise , as it be ; but then I be a parish clerk 's daughter , and could never demean myself to dissent fashion , always save and except Master Thurstan 's , bless he . however , I would be catch once or twice unaware , so this time I think I would be up to it , and I move a dry duster wherever I go , to kneel upon in case he begin when I be in a wet place . by - and - by I think , if the man would pray it would be a blessing , for it would prevent his send his eye after I wherever I go ; for when they take to pray they shut their eye , and quiver th ' lid in a queer kind o ' way they Dissenters do . I can speak pretty plain to you , for you be breed in the Church like mysel ' , and must find it as out o ' the way as I do to be among dissent folk . God forbid I should speak disrespectful of Master Thurstan and Miss Faith , though ; I never think on they as Church or dissenter , but just as Christians . but to come back to Jerry . first , I try always to be clean at his back ; but when he wheel round , so as always to face I , I think I would try a different game . so , say I , ' Master Dixon , I ax your pardon , but I must pipeclay under your chair . will you please to move ? ' well , he move ; and by - and - by I be at he again with the same word ; and at after that , again and again , till he be always move about wi ' his chair behind he , like a snail as carry its house on its back . and the great gaupus never seed that I be pipeclaye the same place twice over . at last I get desperate cross , he be so in my way ; so I make two big cross on the tail of his brown coat ; for you see , whenever he go , up or down , he draw out the tail of his coat from under he , and stick they through the bar of the chair ; and flesh and blood could not resist pipeclaye they for he ; and a pretty brushing he would have , I reckon , to get it off again . well ! at length he clear his throat uncommon loud ; so I spread my duster , and shut my eye all ready ; but when nought come of it , I open my eye a little bit to see what he be about . my word ! if there he be not   down on his knee right face I , star as hard as he could . well ! I think it would be hard work to stand that , if he make a long ado ; so I shut my eye again , and try to think serious , as become what I fancy be come ; but , forgive I ! but I think why could not   the fellow go in and pray wi ' Master Thurstan , as have always a calm spirit ready for prayer , instead o ' I , who have my dresser to scour , let alone an apron to iron . at last he say , say he , ' Sally ! will you oblige I with your hand ? ' so I think it be , maybe , Methodee fashion to pray hand in hand ; and I will not deny but I wish I would wash it well after black - lead the kitchen fire . I think I would well tell he it be not so clean as I could wish , so say I , ' Master Dixon , you shall have it , and welcome , if I may just go and wash them first . ' but , say he , ' my dear Sally , dirty or clean it be all the same to I , see I be only speak in a figuring way . what I be ask on my bended knee be , that you would please to be so kind as to be my wed wife ; week after next will suit I , if it be agreeable to you ! ' my word ! I be up on my foot in an instant ! it be odd now , be not   it ? I never think of take the fellow , and get marry ; for all , I will not deny , I have be think it would be agreeable to be ax . but all at once , I could not   abide the chap . ' Sir , ' say I , try to look shame - face as become the occasion , but for all that , feel a twittering round my mouth that I be afeard might end in a laugh ' Master Dixon , I be obleege to you for the compliment , and thank ye all the same , but I think I would prefer a single life . ' he look mighty take aback ; but in a minute he clear up , and be as sweet as ever . he still keep on his knee , and I wish he would take himself up ; but , I reckon , he think it would give force to his word ; say he , ' think again , my dear Sally . I have   a four - room house , and furniture conformable ; and eighty pound a year . you may never have such a chance again . ' there be truth enough in that , but it be not pretty in the man to say it ; and it put I up a bit . ' as for that , neither you nor I can tell , Master Dixon . you be not the first chap as I have   have down on his knee afore I , ax I to marry he   you see I be think of John Rawson , only I think there be no need to say he be on all four it be truth he be on his knee , you know , and maybe you will not be the last . anyhow , I have   no wish to change my condition just now . ' ' I will wait till Christmas , ' say he . ' I have   a pig as will be ready for kill then , so I must get marry before that . ' well now ! would you believe it ? the pig be a temptation . I have a receipt for cure ham , as Miss Faith would never let I try , say the old way be good enough . however , I resist . say I , very stern , because I feel I would be waver , ' Master Dixon , once for all , pig or no pig , I will not marry you . and if you will take my advice , you will get up off your knee . the flag be but damp yet , and it would be an awkward thing to have rheumatiz just before winter . ' with that he get up , stiff enough . he look as sulky a chap as ever I clap eye on . and as he be so black and cross , I think I would do well   whatever come of the pig   to say ' no ' to he . ' you may live to repent this , ' say he , very red . ' but I will not be too hard upon ye , I will give you another chance . I will let you have the night to think about it , and I will just call in to hear your second thought , after chapel to - morrow . ' well now ! do ever you hear the like ? but that be the way with all of they man , think so much of theirselve , and that it be but ask and have . they have   never have I , though ; and I shall be sixty - one next Martinmas , so there be not much time leave for they to try I , I reckon . well ! when Jeremiah say that , he put I up more than ever , and I say , ' my first thought , second thought , and third thought be all one and the same ; you have   but tempt I once , and that be when you speak of your pig . but of yoursel ' you be nothing to boast on , and so I will bid you good night , and I will keep my manner , or else , if I tell the truth , I should say it have be a great loss of time listen to you . but I will be civil so good night . ' he never say a word , but go off as black as thunder , slam the door after he . the master call I in to prayer , but I can not   say I could put my mind to they , for my heart be beat so . however , it be a comfort to have have an offer of holy matrimony ; and though it fluster I , it make I think more of myself . in the night , I begin to wonder if I have not be cruel and hard to he . you see , I be feverish - like ; and the old song of Barbary Allen would keep run in my head , and I think I be Barbary , and he be young Jemmy Gray , and that maybe he would die for love of I ; and I picture he to mysel ' , lie on his death - bed , with his face turn to the wall , ' wi ' deadly sorrow sigh , ' and I could ha ' pinched mysel ' for have be so like cruel Barbary Allen . and when I get up next day , I find it hard to think on the real Jerry Dixon I have see the night before , apart from the sad and sorrowful Jerry I think on a - dying , when I be between sleep and wake . and for many a day I turn sick , when I hear the pass bell , for I think it be the bell loud - knelling which be to break my heart wi ' a sense of what I have miss in say ' no ' to Jerry , and so kill he with cruelty . but in less than a three week , I hear parish bell a - ring merrily for a wedding ; and in the course of a morning , some one say to I , ' Hark ! how the bell be ring for Jerry Dixon 's wedding ! ' and , all on a sudden , he change back again from a heart - break young fellow , like Jemmy Gray , into a stout , middle - aged man , ruddy - complexion , with a wart on his left cheek like life ! " 

 Sally wait for some exclamation at the conclusion of her tale ; but receive none , she step softly to the bedside , and there lie Ruth , peaceful as death , with her baby on her breast . 

 " I think I would lose some of my gift if I could not talk a body to sleep , " say Sally , in a satisfied and self - complacent tone . 

 Youth be strong and powerful , and make a hard battle against sorrow . so Ruth strove and strengthen , and her baby flourish accordingly ; and before the little celandine be out on the hedge - bank , or the white violet have send forth their fragrance from the border under the south wall of Miss Benson 's small garden , Ruth be able to carry her baby into that shelter place on sunny day . 

 she often wish to thank Mr Benson and his sister , but she do not know how to tell the deep gratitude she feel , and therefore she be silent . but they understand her silence well . one day , as she watch her sleep child , she speak to Miss Benson , with whom she happen to be alone . 

 " do you know of any cottage where the people be clean , and where they would not mind take I in ? " ask she . 

 " take you in ! what do you mean ? " say Miss Benson , drop her knitting , in order to observe Ruth more closely . 

 " I mean , " say Ruth , " where I might lodge with my baby any very poor place would do , only it must be clean , or he might be ill . " 

 " and what in the world do you want to go and lodge in a cottage for ? " say Miss Benson , indignantly . 

 Ruth do not lift up her eye , but she speak with a firmness which show that she have consider the subject . 

 " I think I could make dress . I know I do not learn as much as I might , but perhaps I might do for servant , and people who be not particular . " 

 " servant be as particular as any one , " say Miss Benson , glad to lay hold of the first objection that she could . 

 " well ! somebody who would be patient with I , " say Ruth . 

 " nobody be patient over an ill - fitting gown , " put in Miss Benson . " there be the stuff spoilt , and what not ! " 

 " perhaps I could find plain work to do , " say Ruth , very meekly . " that I can do very well ; mamma teach I , and I like to learn from she . if you would be so good , Miss Benson , you might tell people I could do plain work very neatly , and punctually , and cheaply . " 

 " you would get sixpence a day , perhaps , " say Miss Benson , " and who would take care of baby , I should like to know ? prettily he would be neglect , would not he ? why , he would have the croup and the typhus fever in no time , and be burn to ash after . " 

 " I have think of all . look how he sleep ! Hush , darling ; " for just at this point he begin to cry , and to show his determination to be awake , as if in contradiction to his mother 's word . Ruth take he up , and carry he about the room while she go on speak . 

 " yes , just now I know he will not sleep ; but very often he will , and in the night he always do . " 

 " and so you would work in the night and kill yourself , and leave your poor baby an orphan . Ruth ! I be ashamed of you . now , brother "   Mr Benson have just come in , " be not this too bad of Ruth ; here she be plan to go away and leave we , just as we as I , at least , have grow so fond of baby , and he be begin to know I . " 

 " where be you think of go to , Ruth ? " interrupt Mr Benson , with mild surprise . 

 " anywhere to be near you and Miss Benson ; in any poor cottage where I might lodge very cheaply , and earn my livelihood by take in plain sewing , and perhaps a little dressmaking ; and where I could come and see you and dear Miss Benson sometimes and bring baby . " 

 " if he be not dead before then of some fever , or burn , or scald , poor neglect child ; or you have not work yourself to death with never sleep , " say Miss Benson . 

 Mr Benson think a minute or two , and then he speak to Ruth . 

 " whatever you may do when this little fellow be a year old , and able to dispense with some of a mother 's care , let I beg you , Ruth , as a favour to I as a still great favour to my sister , be it not , Faith ? " 

 " yes ; you may put it so if you like . " 

 " to stay with we , " continue he , " till then . when baby be twelve month old , we will talk about it again , and very likely before then some opening may be show we . never fear lead an idle life , Ruth . we will treat you as a daughter , and set you all the household task ; and it be not for your sake that we ask you to stay , but for this little dumb helpless child 's ; and it be not for our sake that you must stay , but for his . " 

 Ruth be sob . 

 " I do not deserve your kindness , " say she , in a broken voice ; " I do not deserve it . " 

 her tear fall fast and soft like summer rain , but no further word be speak . Mr Benson quietly pass on to make the inquiry for which he have enter the room . 

 but when there be nothing to decide upon , and no necessity for enter upon any new course of action , Ruth 's mind relax from its string - up state . she fall into train of reverie , and mournful regretful recollection which render her languid and tearful . this be notice both by Miss Benson and Sally , and as each have keen sympathy , and feel depressed when they see any one near they depressed , and as each , without much reasoning on the cause or reason for such depression , feel irritated at the uncomfortable state into which they themselves be throw , they both resolve to speak to Ruth on the next fitting occasion . 

 accordingly , one afternoon the morning of that day have be spend by Ruth in housework , for she have insist on Mr Benson 's word , and have take Miss Benson 's share of the more active and fatigue household duty , but she go through they heavily , and as if her heart be far away in the afternoon when she be nurse her child , Sally , on come into the back parlour , find she there alone , and easily detect the fact that she have be cry . 

 " where be Miss Benson ? " say Sally , gruffly . 

 " go out with Mr Benson , " answer Ruth , with an absent sadness in her voice and manner . her tear , scarce check while she speak , begin to fall afresh ; and as Sally stand and gaze she see the babe look back in his mother 's face , and his little lip begin to quiver , and his open blue eye to grow over - clouded , as with some mysterious sympathy with the sorrowful face bent over he . Sally take he briskly from his mother 's arm ; Ruth look up in grave surprise , for in truth she have forget Sally 's presence , and the suddenness of the motion startle she . 

 " my bonny boy ! be they let the salt tear drop on thy sweet face before thou'rt wean ! little somebody know how to be a mother I could make a well myself . ' dance , thumbkin , dance dance , ye merry man every one . ' Aye , that be it ! smile , my pretty . any one but a child like thee , " continue she , turn to Ruth , " would have know well than to bring ill - luck on thy babby by let tear fall on its face before it be wean . but thou'rt not fit to have a babby , and so I have   say many a time . ' I be silent , for , you see , she puzzle I . so she go on , ' what be that beautiful answer in your church catechism , Sally ? ' well ! ' well ! ' just try for a day to think of all the odd job as have to be do well and truly as in God 's sight , not just slur over anyhow , and you will go through they twice as cheerfully , and have no thought to spare for sigh or cry . "

 CHAPTER XVII 

 Leonard 's christening 
 

 in that body of Dissenters to which Mr Benson belong , it be not consider necessary to baptize infant as early as the ceremony can be perform ; and many circumstance concur to cause the solemn thanksgiving and dedication of the child   for so these dissenter look upon christening   to be defer until it be probably somewhere about six month old . there have be many conversation in the little sit - room between the brother and sister and their protegťe , which have consist more of question betray a thoughtful wonder kind of ignorance on the part of Ruth , and answer more suggestive than explanatory from Mr Benson ; while Miss Benson keep up a kind of running commentary , always simple and often quaint , but with that intuition into the very heart of all thing truly religious which be often the gift of those who seem , at first sight , to be only affectionate and sensible . when Mr Benson have explain his own view of what a christening ought to be consider , and , by call out Ruth 's latent feeling into pious earnestness , bring she into a right frame of mind , he feel that he have do what he could to make the ceremony more than a mere form , and to invest it , quiet , humble , and obscure as it must necessarily be in outward shape mournful and anxious as much of its antecedent have render it with the severe grandeur of an act do in faith and truth .

 CHAPTER xviii 

 Ruth become a Governess in Mr Bradshaw 's Family 
 

 one afternoon , not long after this , Mr and Miss Benson set off to call upon a farmer , who attend the chapel , but live at some distance from the town . they intend to stay to tea if they be invite , and Ruth and Sally be leave to spend a long afternoon together . at first , Sally be busy in her kitchen , and Ruth employ herself in carry her baby out into the garden . it be now nearly a year since she come to the benson ' ; it seem like yesterday , and yet as if a lifetime have go between . the flower be bud now , that be all in bloom when she come down , on the first autumnal morning , into the sunny parlour . the yellow jessamine , that be then a tender plant , have now take firm root in the soil , and be send out strong shoot ; the wall - flower , which Miss Benson have sow on the wall a day or two after her arrival , be scent the air with their fragrant flower . Ruth know every plant now ; it seem as though she have always live here , and always know the inhabitant of the house . she hear Sally sing her accustomed song in the kitchen , a song she never vary over her afternoon 's work . it begin , 
 

 as I be go to Derby , sir , 
 upon a market - day . 
 

 and if music be a necessary element in a song , perhaps I have well call it by some other name .
