 CHAPTER XIX 

 after five year 
 

 the quiet day grow into week and month , and even year , without any event to startle the little circle into the consciousness of the lapse of time . one who have know they at the date of Ruth 's become a governess in Mr Bradshaw 's family , and have be absent until the time of which I be now go to tell you , would have note some change which have imperceptibly come over all ; but he , too , would have think , that the life which have bring so little of turmoil and vicissitude must have be calm and tranquil , and in accordance with the bygone activity of the town in which their existence pass away . 

 the alteration that he would have perceive be those cause by the natural progress of time . the Benson home be brighten into vividness by the presence of the little Leonard , now a noble boy of six , large and grand in limb and stature , and with a face of marked beauty and intelligence . indeed , he might have be consider by many as too intelligent for his year ; and often the living with old and thoughtful people give he , beyond most child , the appearance of ponder over the mystery which meet the young on the threshold of life , but which fade away as advance year bring we more into contact with the practical and tangible fade away and vanish , until it seem to require the agitation of some great storm of the soul before we can again realise spiritual thing . 

 but , at time , Leonard seem oppress and bewilder , after listening intent , with grave and wonder eye , to the conversation around he ; at other , the bright animal life shine forth radiant , and no three - month ' kitten no foal , suddenly toss up its heel by the side of its sedate dam , and career around the pasture in pure mad enjoyment no young creature of any kind , could show more merriment and gladness of heart . 

 " for ever in mischief , " be Sally 's account of he at such time ; but it be not intentional mischief ; and Sally herself would have be the first to scold any one else who have use the same word in reference to her darling . indeed , she be once nearly give warning , because she think the boy be be ill - use . the occasion be this : Leonard have for some time show a strange , odd disregard of truth ; he invent story , and tell they with so grave a face , that unless there be some internal evidence of their incorrectness   such as describe a cow with a bonnet on , he be generally believe , and his statement , which be give with the full appearance of relate a real occurrence , have once or twice lead to awkward result . all the three , whose heart be pain by this apparent unconsciousness of the difference between truth and falsehood , be unaccustomed to child , or they would have recognise this as a stage through which most infant , who have lively imagination , pass ; and , accordingly , there be a consultation in Mr Benson 's study one morning . Ruth be there , quiet , very pale , and with compress lip , sick at heart as she hear Miss Benson 's argument for the necessity of whipping , in order to cure Leonard of his story - telling . " he go into the garden , and deliberately , almost as if he wish to gain time , choose and cut off a little switch from the laburnum - tree . then he return through the kitchen , and gravely take the awed and wonder little fellow by the hand , he lead he silently into the study , and place he before he , begin an admonition on the importance of truthfulness , mean to conclude with what he believe to be the moral of all punishment : " as you can not remember this of yourself , I must give you a little pain to make you remember it . I be very sorry it be necessary , and that you can not recollect without my do so . "

 " and what may ye be go to do with that fine switch I see ye gathering , Master Thurstan ? " ask she , her eye gleam with anger at the answer she know must come , if answer she have at all .

I will be good I make a promise ; I will speak true I make a promise . " and he keep his word . 

 Miss Benson pique herself upon be less carry away by her love for this child than any one else in the house ; she talk severely , and have capital theory ; but her severity end in talk , and her theory would not work . however , she read several book on education , knit sock for Leonard all the while ; and , upon the whole , I think , the hand be more usefully employ than the head , and the good honest heart well than either . she look old than when we first know she , but it be a ripe , kindly age that be come over she . her excellent practical sense , perhaps , make she a more masculine character than her brother . he be often so much perplex by the problem of life , that he let the time for action go by ; but she keep he in check by her clear , pithy talk , which bring back his wander thought to the duty that lie straight before he , wait for action ; and then he remember that it be the faithful part to " wait patiently upon God , " and leave the end in his hand , who alone know why evil exist in this world , and why it ever hover on either side of Good . in this respect , Miss Benson have more faith than her brother or so it seem ; for quick , resolute action in the next step of life be all she require , while he deliberate and tremble , and often do wrong from his very deliberation , when his first instinct would have lead he right . 

 but although decide and prompt as ever , Miss Benson be grow old since the summer afternoon when she dismount from the coach at the foot of the long Welsh hill that lead to Llan - dhu , where her brother await she to consult she about Ruth . though her eye be as bright and straight - look as ever , quick and brave in its glance , her hair have become almost snowy white ; and it be on this point she consult Sally , soon after the date of Leonard 's last untruth . the two be arrange Miss Benson 's room one morning , when , after dust the look - glass , she suddenly stop in her operation , and after a close inspection of herself , startle Sally by this speech : 

 " Sally ! I be look a great deal old than I use to do ! " 

 Sally , who be busy dilate on the increase price of flour , consider this remark of Miss Benson 's as strangely irrelevant to the matter in hand , and only notice it by a 

 " to be sure ! I suppose we all on we do . but two - and - fourpence a dozen be too much to make we pay for it . " 

 Miss Benson go on with her inspection of herself , and Sally with her economical project . 

 " Sally ! " say Miss Benson , " my hair be nearly white . the last time I look it be only pepper - and - salt . what must I do ? " 

 " do why , what would the wench do ? " ask Sally , contemptuously . " Ye're never go to be take in , at your time of life , by hair - dye and such gimcrack , as can only take in young girl whose wisdom - tooth be not cut . " 

 " and who be not very likely to want they , " say Miss Benson , quietly . " no ! but you see , Sally , it be very awkward have such grey hair , and feel so young . do you know , Sally , I have   as great a mind for dancing , when I hear a lively tune on the street - organ , as ever ; and as great a mind to sing when I be happy to sing in my old way , Sally , you know . " 

 " Aye , you have it from a girl , " say Sally ; " and many a time , when the door 's be shut , I do not know if it be you in the parlour , or a big bumble - bee in the kitchen , as be make that drumbling noise . I hear you at it yesterday . " 

 " but an old woman with grey hair ought not to have a fancy for dancing or singing , " continue Miss Benson . 

 " Whatten nonsense be ye talk ? " say Sally , rouse to indignation . " call yoursel ' an old woman when you be well than ten year young than I ! and many a girl have grey hair at five - and - twenty . " 

 " but I be more than five - and - twenty , Sally . I be fifty - seven next May ! " 

 " More shame for ye , then , not to know well than to talk of dye your hair . I can not abide such vanity ! " 

 " oh , dear ! Sally , when will you understand what I mean ? I want to know how I be to keep remember how old I be , so as to prevent myself from feel so young ? I be quite startled just now to see my hair in the glass , for I can generally tell if my cap be straight by feel . I will tell you what I will do I will cut off a piece of my grey hair , and plait it together for a marker in my Bible ! " Miss Benson expect applause for this bright idea , but Sally only make answer : 

 " you will be take to paint your cheek next , now you have   once think of dye your hair . " so Miss Benson plait her grey hair in silence and quietness , Leonard hold one end of it while she weave it , and admire the colour and texture all the time , with a sort of imply dissatisfaction at the auburn colour of his own curl , which be only half - comfort away by Miss Benson 's information , that , if he live long enough , his hair would be like her .

 CHAPTER XXII 

 the Liberal Candidate and his Precursor 
 

 Jemima do not know whether she wish to go to Abermouth or not . she long for change . she weary of the sight and sound of home . but yet she could not bear to leave the neighbourhood of Mr Farquhar ; especially as , if she go to Abermouth , Ruth would in all probability be leave to take her holiday at home . 

 when Mr Bradshaw decide that she be to go , Ruth try to feel glad that he give she the mean of repair her fault towards Elizabeth ; and she resolve to watch over the two girl most faithfully and carefully , and to do all in her power to restore the invalid to health . but a tremor come over she whenever she think of leave Leonard ; she have never quit he for a day , and it seem to she as if her brooding , constant care be his natural and necessary shelter from all evil from very death itself . she would not go to sleep at night , in order to enjoy the blessed consciousness of have he near she ; when she be away from he teach her pupil , she keep try to remember his face , and print it deep on her heart , against the time when day and day would elapse without her see that little darling countenance . Miss Benson would wonder to her brother that Mr Bradshaw do not propose that Leonard should accompany his mother ; he only beg she not to put such an idea into Ruth 's head , as he be sure Mr Bradshaw have no thought of do any such thing , yet to Ruth it might be a hope , and then a disappointment . his sister scold he for be so cold - hearted ; but he be full of sympathy , although he do not express it , and make some quiet little sacrifice in order to set himself at liberty to take Leonard a long walk expedition on the day when his mother leave Eccleston . 

 Ruth cry until she could cry no long , and feel very much ashamed of herself as she see the grave and wonder look of her pupil , whose only feeling on leave home be delight at the idea of Abermouth , and into whose mind the possibility of death to any of their beloved one never enter . Ruth dry her eye , and speak cheerfully as soon as she catch the perplexed expression of their face ; and by the time they arrive at Abermouth , she be as much delighted with all the new scenery as they be , and find it hard work to resist their entreaty to go ramble out on the seashore at once ; but Elizabeth have undergo more fatigue that day than she have have before for many week , and Ruth be determined to be prudent . 

 meanwhile , the Bradshaws ' house at Eccleston be be rapidly adapt for electioneer hospitality . the partition - wall between the unused drawing - room and the school - room be break down , in order to admit of fold door ; the " ingenious " upholsterer of the town   and what town do not boast of the upholsterer full of contrivance and resource , in opposition to the upholsterer of steady capital and no imagination , who look down with uneasy contempt on ingenuity ?   have come in to give his opinion , that " nothing could be easy than to convert a bathroom into a bedroom , by the assistance of a little drapery to conceal the shower - bath , " the string of which be to be carefully conceal , for fear that the unconscious occupier of the bath - bed might innocently take it for a bell - rope . the professional cook of the town have be already engage to take up her abode for a month at Mr Bradshaw 's , much to the indignation of Betsy , who become a vehement partisan of Mr Cranworth , as soon as ever she hear of the plan of her deposition from sovereign authority in the kitchen , in which she have reign supreme for fourteen year . Mrs Bradshaw sigh and bemoan herself in all her leisure moment , which be not many , and wonder why their house be to be turn into an inn for this Mr Donne , when everybody know that the George be good enough for the Cranworths , who never think of ask the elector to the Hall ; and they have live at cranworth ever since Julius Caesar 's time , and if that be not be an old family , she do not know what be . the excitement soothe Jemima . there be something to do . it be she who plan with the upholsterer ; it be she who soothe Betsy into angry silence ; it be she who persuade her mother to lie down and rest , while she herself go out to buy the heterogeneous thing require to make the family and house presentable to Mr Donne and his precursor the friend of the parliamentary agent . this latter gentleman never appear himself on the scene of action , but pull all the string notwithstanding . the friend be a Mr Hickson , a lawyer a briefless barrister , some people call he ; but he himself profess a great disgust to the law , as a " great sham , " which involve an immensity of underhand action , and truckling , and time - serve , and be perfectly encumber by useless form and ceremony , and dead obsolete word . so , instead of put his shoulder to the wheel to reform the law , he talk eloquently against it , in such a high - priest style , that it be occasionally a matter of surprise how he could ever have make a friend of the parliamentary agent before mention . but , as Mr Hickson himself say , it be the very corruptness of the law which he be fight against , in do all he could to effect the return of certain member to Parliament ; these certain member be pledge to effect a reform in the law , accord to Mr Hickson . and , as he once observe confidentially , " if you have to destroy a hydra - head monster , would you measure sword with the demon as if he be a gentleman ? would you not rather seize the first weapon that come to hand ? and so do I. my great object in life , sir , be to reform the law of England , sir . once get a majority of liberal member into the House , and the thing be do . and I consider myself justify , for so high for , I may say , so holy an end , in use man 's weakness to work out my purpose . of course , if man be angel , or even immaculate man invulnerable to bribe , we would not bribe . " 

 " could you ? " ask Jemima , for the conversation take place at Mr Bradshaw 's dinner - table , where a few friend be gather together to meet Mr Hickson ; and among they be Mr Benson . 

 " we neither would nor could , " say the ardent barrister , disregard in his vehemence the point of the question , and float on over the bar of argument into the wide ocean of his own eloquence : " as it be as the world stand , they who would succeed even in good deed must come down to the level of expediency ; and therefore , I say once more , if Mr Donne be the man for your purpose , and your purpose be a good one , a lofty one , a holy one "   for Mr Hickson remember the dissenting character of his little audience , and privately consider the introduction of the word " holy " a most happy hit , " then , I say , we must put all the squeamish scruple which might befit Utopia , or some such place , on one side , and treat man as they be . if they be avaricious , it be not we who have make they so ; but as we have to do with they , we must consider their failing in deal with they ; if they have be careless or extravagant , or have have their little peccadillo , we must administer the screw . the glorious reform of the law will justify , in my idea , all mean to obtain the end that law , from the profession of which I have withdraw myself from perhaps a too scrupulous conscience ! " he conclude softly to himself . 

 " we be not to do evil that good may come , " say Mr Benson . he be startle at the deep sound of his own voice as he utter these word ; but he have not be speak for some time , and his voice come forth strong and unmodulated . 

 " true , sir ; most true , " say Mr Hickson , bow . " I honour you for the observation . " and he profit by it , insomuch that he confine his further remark on election to the end of the table , where he sit near Mr Bradshaw , and one or two equally eager , though not equally influential partisan of Mr Donne 's . meanwhile , Mr Farquhar take up Mr Benson 's quotation , at the end where he and Jemima sit near to Mrs Bradshaw and he . 

 " but in the present state of the world , as Mr Hickson say , it be rather difficult to act upon that precept . " 

 " oh , Mr Farquhar ! " say Jemima , indignantly , the tear spring to her eye with a feeling of disappointment . for she have be chafe under all that Mr Hickson have be say , perhaps the more for one or two attempt on his part at a flirtation with the daughter of his wealthy host , which she resent with all the loathing of a pre - occupied heart ; and she have long to be a man , to speak out her wrath at this paltering with right and wrong . she have feel grateful to Mr Benson for his one clear , short precept , come down with a divine force against which there be no appeal ; and now to have Mr Farquhar take the side of expediency ! it be too bad . 

 " Nay , Jemima ! " say Mr Farquhar , touch , and secretly flatter by the visible pain his speech have give . " do not   be indignant with I till I have explain myself a little more . I do not   understand myself yet ; and it be a very intricate question , or so it appear to I , which I be go to put , really , earnestly , and humbly , for Mr Benson 's opinion . now , Mr Benson , may I ask , if you always find it practicable to act strictly in accordance with that principle ? for if you do not , I be sure no man live can ! be there not occasion when it be absolutely necessary to wade through evil to good ? I be not speak in the careless , presumptuous way of that man yonder , " say he , lower his voice , and address himself to Jemima more exclusively ; " I be really anxious to hear what Mr Benson will say on the subject , for I know no one to whose candid opinion I should attach more weight . " 

 but Mr Benson be silent . he do not see Mrs Bradshaw and Jemima leave the room . he be really , as Mr Farquhar suppose he , completely absent , question himself as to how far his practice tally with his principle . by degree he come to himself ; he find the conversation still turn on the election ; and Mr Hickson , who feel that he have jar against the little minister 's principle , and yet know , from the carte du pay which the scout of the parliamentary agent have give he , that Mr Benson be a person to be conciliate , on account of his influence over many of the work people , begin to ask he question with an air of defer to superior knowledge , that almost surprise Mr Bradshaw , who have be accustom to treat " Benson " in a very different fashion , of civil condescending indulgence , just as one listen to a child who can have have no opportunity of know well . 

 at the end of a conversation that Mr Hickson hold with Mr Benson , on a subject in which the latter be really interested , and on which he have express himself at some length , the young barrister turn to Mr Bradshaw , and say very audibly , 

 " I wish Donne have be here . this conversation during the last half - hour would have interest he almost as much as it have do I . " 

 Mr Bradshaw little guess the truth , that Mr Donne be , at that very moment , coach up the various subject of public interest in Eccleston , and privately curse the particular subject on which Mr Benson have be hold forth , as be an unintelligible piece of Quixotism ; or the lead Dissenter of the town need not have experience a pang of jealousy at the possible future admiration his minister might excite in the possible future member for Eccleston . and if Mr Benson have be clairvoyant , he need not have make an especial subject of gratitude out of the likelihood that he might have an opportunity of so far interesting Mr Donne in the condition of the people of Eccleston as to induce he to set his face against any attempt at bribery . 

 Mr Benson think of this half the night through ; and end by determine to write a sermon on the christian view of political duty , which might be good for all , both elector and member , to hear on the eve of an election . for Mr Donne be expect at Mr Bradshaw 's before the next Sunday ; and , of course , as Mr and Miss Benson have settle it , he would appear at the chapel with they on that day . but the stinging conscience refuse to be quiet . no present plan of usefulness allay the aching remembrance of the evil he have do that good might come . not even the look of Leonard , as the early dawn fall on he , and Mr Benson 's sleepless eye see the rosy glow on his firm round cheek ; his open mouth , through which the soft , long - draw breath come gently quiver ; and his eye not fully shut , but close to outward sight not even the aspect of the quiet , innocent child could soothe the troubled spirit . 

 Leonard and his mother dream of each other that night . her dream of he be one of undefined terror terror so great that it waken she up , and she strove not to sleep again , for fear that ominous ghastly dream should return . he , on the contrary , dream of her sit watch and smile by his bedside , as her gentle self have be many a morning ; and when she see he awake   so it fall out in the dream , she smile still more sweetly , and bend down she kiss he , and then spread out large , soft , white - feather wing   which in no way surprise her child he seem to have know they be there all along , and sail away through the open window far into the blue sky of a summer 's day . Leonard waken up then , and remember how far away she really be far more distant and inaccessible than the beautiful blue sky to which she have betake herself in his dream and cry himself to sleep again .

 it be a large house , build on the summit of a rock , which nearly overhang the shore below ; there be , to be sure , a series of zigzag tacking path down the face of this rock , but from the house they could not be see . old or delicate people would have consider the situation bleak and expose ; indeed , the present proprietor want to dispose of it on this very account ; but by its present inhabitant , this exposure and bleakness be call by other name , and consider as charm . from every part of the room they see the grey storm gather on the sea - horizon , and put themselves in march array ; and soon the march become a sweep , and the great dome of the heaven be cover with the lurid cloud , between which and the vivid green earth below there seem to come a purple atmosphere , make the very threatening beautiful ; and by - and - by the house be wrap in sheet of rain shut out sky , and sea , and inland view ; till , of a sudden , the storm be go by , and the heavy rain - drop glisten in the sun as they hang on leaf and grass , and the " little bird sing east , and the little bird sing west , " and there be a pleasant sound of running water all abroad .

in this one case bribery must be allow be allowable ; but it be a great pity human nature be so corrupt , and if his member succeed , he would double his subscription to the school , in order that the next generation might be teach well . there be various other reason , which strengthen Mr Bradshaw in the bright idea of go down to Abermouth for the Sunday ; some connect with the out - of - door politic , and some with the domestic . for instance , it have be the plan of the house to have a cold dinner on the Sundays Mr Bradshaw have pique himself on this strictness and yet he have an instinctive feeling that Mr Donne be not quite the man to partake of cold meat for conscience ' sake with cheerful indifference to his fare .

I shall let it be clearly understand from the husting , that I most decidedly disapprove of bribery , and leave the rest to Hickson 's management . he be accustomed to these sort of thing . I be not . " 

 Mr Bradshaw be rather perplex by this want of bustle energy on the part of the new candidate ; and if it have not be for the four thousand pound aforesaid , would have doubt whether Mr Donne care sufficiently for the result of the election . Jemima think differently . she watch her father 's visitor attentively , with something like the curious observation which a naturalist bestow on a new specie of animal .

 " not any person not any human being , mamma , " say Jemima , half smile . " do you remember our stop at Wakefield once , on our way to Scarborough , and there be horse - race go on somewhere , and some of the racer be in the stable at the inn where we din ? "

 " why , Richard , somehow , know one of the jockey , and , as we be come in from our ramble through the town , this man , or boy , ask we to look at one of the racer he have the charge of . " 

 " well , my dear ! " 

 " well , mamma ! Mr Donne be like that horse ! " 

 " Nonsense , Jemima ; you must not say so . I do not   know what your father would say , if he hear you liken Mr Donne to a brute . "

I can see your papa stand by , ready to shake they to get out their news . " 

 " but Mr Donne 's question be always to the point , and force out the grain without the chaff . and look at he , if any one tell he ill news about the election ! have you never see a dull red light come into his eye ? that be like my race - horse . her flesh quiver all over , at certain sound and noise which have some meaning to she ; but she stand quite still , pretty creature ! now , Mr Donne be just as eager as she be , though he may be too proud to show it . though he seem so gentle , I almost think he be very headstrong in follow out his own will . " 

 " well ! do not   call he like a horse again , for I be sure papa would not like it . do you know , I think you be go to say he be like little Leonard , when you ask I who he be like . " 

 " Leonard ! oh , mamma , he be not in the least like Leonard . he be twenty time more like my race - horse . 

 " now , my dear Jemima , do be quiet . your father think race so wrong , that I be sure he would be very seriously displeased if he be to hear you . " 

 to return to Mr Bradshaw , and to give one more of his various reason for wish to take Mr Donne to Abermouth . the wealthy Eccleston manufacturer be uncomfortably impressed with an indefinable sense of inferiority to his visitor . it be not in education , for Mr Bradshaw be a well - educate man ; it be not in power , for , if he choose , the present object of Mr Donne 's life might be utterly defeat ; it do not arise from anything overbear in manner , for Mr Donne be habitually polite and courteous , and be just now anxious to propitiate his host , whom he look upon as a very useful man . whatever this sense of inferiority arise from , Mr Bradshaw be anxious to relieve himself of it , and imagine that if he could make more display of his wealth his object would be obtain . now his house in Eccleston be old - fashioned , and ill - calculate to exhibit money 's worth . his mode of living , though strain to a high pitch just at this time , he become aware be no more than Mr Donne be accustom to every day of his life . the first day at dessert , some remark   some opportune remark , as Mr Bradshaw in his innocence have think   be make regard the price of pine - apple , which be rather exorbitant that year , and Mr Donne ask Mrs Bradshaw , with quiet surprise , if they have no pinery , as if to be without a pinery be indeed a depth of pitiable destitution . in fact , Mr Donne have be bear and cradle in all that wealth could purchase , and so have his ancestor before he for so many generation , that refinement and luxury seem the natural condition of man , and they that dwelt without be in the position of monster . the absence be notice ; but not the presence .

 all these mingle motif cause the determination which make Ruth sit in the little inn - parlour at Abermouth during the wild storm 's passage .

 " oh , how charming ! then we shall see this new member after all ! " while Elizabeth add , 

 " yes ! I shall like to do that . but where must we be ? papa will want the dining - room and this room , and where must we sit ? "

 CHAPTER XXIII 

 Recognition 
 

 Saturday come . tear , ragged cloud be drive across the sky . it be not a become day for the scenery , and the little girl regret it much . first they hop for a change at twelve o'clock , and then at the afternoon tide - turning . but at neither time do the sun show his face . 

 " Papa will never buy this dear place , " say Elizabeth , sadly , as she watch the weather . " the sun be everything to it . the sea look quite leaden to - day , and there be no sparkle on it . and the sand , that be so yellow and sun - speckle on Thursday , be all one dull brown now . " 

 " never mind ! to - morrow may be well , " say Ruth , cheerily . 

 " I wonder what time they will come at ? " inquire Mary . 

 " your papa say they would be at the station at five o'clock . and the landlady at the Swan say it would take they half an hour to get here . " 

 " and they be to dine at six ? " ask Elizabeth . 

 " yes , " answer Ruth . " and I think if we have our tea half an hour early , at half - past four , and then go out for a walk , we should be nicely out of the way just during the bustle of the arrival and dinner ; and we could be in the drawing - room ready against your papa come in after dinner . " 

 " oh ! that would be nice , " say they ; and tea be order accordingly . 

 the south - westerly wind have drop , and the cloud be stationary , when they go out on the sand . they dig little hole near the in - come tide , and make canal to they from the water , and blow the light sea - foam against each other ; and then steal on tiptoe near to the group of grey and white sea - gull , which despise their caution , fly softly and slowly away to a little distance as soon as they draw near . and in all this Ruth be as great a child as any . only she long for Leonard with a mother 's longing , as indeed she do every day , and all hour of the day . by - and - by the cloud thicken yet more , and one or two drop of rain be feel . it be very little , but Ruth fear a shower for her delicate Elizabeth , and besides , the September evening be fast closing in the dark and sunless day . as they turn homeward in the rapidly increase dusk , they see three figure on the sand near the rock , come in their direction . 

 " Papa and Mr Donne ! " exclaim Mary . " now we shall see he ! " 

 " which do you make out be he ? " ask Elizabeth . 

 " oh ! the tall one , to be sure . do not   you see how papa always turn to he , as if he be speak to he and not to the other ? " 

 " who be the other ? " ask Elizabeth . 

 " Mr Bradshaw say that Mr Farquhar and Mr Hickson would come with he . but that be not Mr Farquhar , I be sure , " say Ruth . 

 the girl look at each other , as they always do , when Ruth mention Mr Farquhar 's name ; but she be perfectly unconscious both of the look and of the conjecture which give rise to it . 

 as soon as the two party draw near , Mr Bradshaw call out in his strong voice , 

 " well , my dear ! we find there be an hour before dinner , so we come down upon the sand , and here you be . " 

 the tone of his voice assure they that he be in a bland and indulgent mood , and the two little girl run towards he . he kiss they , and shake hand with Ruth ; tell his companion that these be the little girl who be tempt he to this extravagance of purchase Eagle 's Crag ; and then , rather doubtfully , and because he see that Mr Donne expect it , he introduce " my daughter ' governess , Mrs Denbigh . " 

 it be grow dark every moment , and it be time they should hasten back to the rock , which be even now indistinct in the grey haze . Mr Bradshaw hold a hand of each of his daughter , and Ruth walk alongside , the two strange gentleman be on the outskirt of the party . 

 Mr Bradshaw begin to give his little girl some home news . he tell they that Mr Farquhar be ill , and could not accompany they ; but Jemima and their mamma be quite well . 

 the gentleman near to Ruth speak to she . 

 " be you fond of the sea ? " ask he . there be no answer , so he repeat his question in a different form . 

 " do you enjoy stay by the seaside ? I should rather ask . " 

 the reply be " yes , " rather breathe out in a deep inspiration than speak in a sound . the sand heave and tremble beneath Ruth . the figure near she vanish into strange nothingness ; the sound of their voice be as distant sound in a dream , while the echo of one voice thrill through and through . she could have catch at his arm for support , in the awful dizziness which wrap she up , body and soul . that voice ! no ! if name , and face , and figure be all change , that voice be the same which have touch her girlish heart , which have speak most tender word of love , which have win , and wreck she , and which she have last hear in the low muttering of fever . she dare not look round to see the figure of he who speak , dark as it be . she know he be there she hear he speak in the manner in which he use to address stranger year ago ; perhaps she answer he , perhaps she do not God know . it seem as if weight be tie to her foot as if the steadfast rock recede as if time stand still ; it be so long , so terrible , that path across the reeling sand . 

 at the foot of the rock they separate . Mr Bradshaw , afraid lest dinner should cool , prefer the short way for himself and his friend . on Elizabeth 's account , the girl be to take the long and easy path , which wound upwards through a rocky field , where lark ' nest abound , and where wild thyme and heather be now throw out their sweet to the soft night air . 

 the little girl speak in eager discussion of the stranger . they appeal to Ruth , but Ruth do not answer , and they be too impatient to convince each other to repeat the question . the first little ascent from the sand to the field surmount , Ruth sit down suddenly and cover her face with her hand . this be so unusual their wish , their good , be so invariably the rule of motion or of rest in their walk that the girl , suddenly check , stand silent and affright in surprise . they be still more startled when Ruth wail aloud some inarticulate word . 

 " be you not well , dear Mrs Denbigh ? " ask Elizabeth , gently , kneel down on the grass by Ruth . 

 she sit face the west . the low watery twilight be on her face as she take her hand away . so pale , so haggard , so wild and wander a look the girl have never see on human countenance before . 

 " well ! what be you do here with I ? you should not be with I , " say she , shake her head slowly . 

 they look at each other . 

 " you be sadly tired , " say Elizabeth , soothingly . " come home , and let I help you to bed . I will tell papa you be ill , and ask he to send for a doctor . " 

 Ruth look at she as if she do not understand the meaning of her word . no more she do at first . but by - and - by the dull brain begin to think most vividly and rapidly , and she speak in a sharp way which deceive the girl into a belief that nothing have be the matter . 

 " yes ! I be tired . I be tired . those sand oh ! those sand , those weary , dreadful sand ! but that be all over now . only my heart ache still . feel how it flutter and beat , " say she , take Elizabeth 's hand , and hold it to her side . " I be quite well , though , " she continue , read pity in the child 's look , as she feel the trembling , quiver beat . " we will go straight to the dressing - room , and read a chapter ; that will still my heart ; and then I will go to bed , and Mr Bradshaw will excuse I , I know , this one night . I only ask for one night . put on your right frock , dear , and do all you ought to do . but I know you will , " say she , bend down to kiss Elizabeth , and then , before she have do so , raise her head abruptly . " you be good and dear girl God keep you so ! " 

 by a strong effort at self - command , she go onwards at an even pace , neither rush nor pause to sob and think . the very regularity of motion calm she . the front and back door of the house be on two side , at right angle with each other . they all shrunk a little from the idea of go in at the front door , now that the strange gentleman be about , and , accordingly , they go through the quiet farm - yard right into the bright , ruddy kitchen , where the servant be dash about with the dinner thing . it be a contrast in more than colour to the lonely , dusky field , which even the little girl perceive ; and the noise , the warmth , the very bustle of the servant , be a positive relief to Ruth , and for the time lift off the heavy press of pen - up passion . a silent house , with moonlit room , or with a faint gloom brood over the apartment , would have be more to be dread . then , she must have give way , and cry out . as it be , she go up the old awkward back stair , and into the room they be to sit in . there be no candle . Mary volunteer to go down for one ; and when she return she be full of the wonder of preparation in the drawing - room , and ready and eager to dress , so as to take her place there before the gentleman have finish dinner . but she be strike by the strange paleness of Ruth 's face , now that the light fall upon it . 

 " stay up here , dear Mrs Denbigh ! we will tell papa you be tired , and be go to bed . " 

 another time Ruth would have dread Mr Bradshaw 's displeasure ; for it be an understand thing that no one be to be ill or tired in his household without leave ask , and cause give and assign . but she never think of that now . her great desire be to hold quiet till she be alone . quietness it be not it be rigidity ; but she succeed in be rigid in look and movement , and go through her duty to Elizabeth   who prefer remain with her upstairs   with wooden precision . but her heart feel at time like ice , at time like burn fire ; always a heavy , heavy weight within she . at last Elizabeth go to bed . still Ruth dare not think . Mary would come upstairs soon ; and with a strange , sick , shrink yearning , Ruth await she and the crumb of intelligence she might drop out about he . Ruth 's sense of hearing be quicken to miserable intensity as she stand before the chimney - piece , grasp it tight with both hand gaze into the die fire , but see not the dead grey ember , or the little spark of vivid light that run hither and thither among the wood - ash but an old farm - house , and climb , wind road , and a little golden breezy common , with a rural inn on the hill - top , far , far away . and through the thought of the past come the sharp sound of the present of three voice , one of which be almost silence , it be so hush . indifferent people would only have guess that Mr Donne be speak by the quietness in which the other listen ; but Ruth hear the voice and many of the word , though they convey no idea to her mind . she be too much stunned even to feel curious to know to what they relate . he speak . that be her one fact .

Mr Hickson be so clever ! she do not know what to make of Mr Donne , he seem such a dawdle . but he be very handsome . have Ruth see he ? oh , no ! she could not , it be so dark on those stupid sand . well , never mind , she would see he to - morrow . she must be well to - morrow . Papa seem a good deal put out that neither she nor Elizabeth be in the drawing - room to - night ; and his last word be , " tell Mrs Denbigh I hope "   and papa 's " hope " always mean " expect "   ' she will be able to make breakfast at nine o'clock ; " and then she would see Mr Donne . 

 that be all Ruth hear about he . she go with Mary into her bedroom , help she to undress , and put the candle out . at length she be alone in her own room ! at length ! 

 but the tension do not give way immediately . she fasten her door , and throw open the window , cold and threatening as be the night . she tear off her gown ; she put her hair back from her heated face . it seem now as if she could not think as if thought and emotion have be repress so sternly that they would not come to relieve her stupified brain . till all at once , like a flash of lightning , her life , past and present , be reveal to she in its minute detail . and when she see she very present " now , " the strange confusion of agony be too great to be bear , and she cry aloud . then she be quite dead , and listen as to the sound of gallop army . 

 " if I might see he ! if I might see he ! if I might just ask he why he leave I ; if I have vex he in any way ; it be so strange so cruel ! it be not he ; it be his mother , " say she , almost fiercely , as if answer herself . " oh , God ! but he might have find I out before this , " she continue , sadly . " he do not care for I , as I do for he . he do not care for I at all , " she go on wildly and sharply . " he do I cruel harm . I can never again lift up my face in innocence . they think I have forget all , because I do not speak . oh , darling love ! be I talk against you ? " ask she , tenderly . " I be so torn and perplexed ! you , who be the father of my child ! "

 and then she start up , for all this time she have be rock herself backwards and forwards as she sit on the ground , and begin to pace the room with hurried step . 

 " what be I think of ? where be I ? I who have be pray these year and year to be worthy to be Leonard 's mother . my God ! what a depth of sin be in my heart ! why , the old time would be as white as snow to what it would be now , if I seek he out , and pray for the explanation , which should re - establish he in my heart . I who have strive   or make a mock of try   to learn God 's holy will , in order to bring up Leonard into the full strength of a Christian I who have teach his sweet innocent lip to pray , ' lead we not into temptation , but deliver we from evil ; ' and yet , somehow , I have   be long to give he to his father , who be who be " she almost choke , till at last she cry sharp out , " oh , my God ! I do believe Leonard 's father be a bad man , and yet , oh ! pitiful God , I love he ; I can not forget I can not ! "

 " I wonder if my darling be frightened with this blustering , noisy wind . I wonder if he be awake . " 

 and then her thought go back to the various time of old , when , affright by the weather sound so mysterious in the night he have creep into her bed and clung to she , and she have soothe he , and sweetly awe he into stillness and childlike faith , by tell he of the goodness and power of God .

 " oh , my God , help I , for I be very weak . my God ! I pray Thee be my rock and my strong fortress , for I of myself be nothing . if I ask in his name , thou wilt give it I . in the name of Jesus Christ I pray for strength to do Thy will ! " 

 she could not think , or , indeed , remember anything but that she be weak , and God be strong , and " a very present help in time of trouble ; " and the wind rise yet higher , and the house shake and vibrate as , in measured time , the great and terrible gust come from the four quarter of the heaven and blow around it , die away in the distance with loud and unearthly wail , which be not utterly still before the sound of the come blast be hear like the trumpet of the vanguard of the Prince of Air . 

 there be a knock at the bedroom door a little , gentle knock , and a soft child 's voice . 

 " Mrs Denbigh , may I come in , please ? I be so frightened ! "

 " oh , Mrs Denbigh ! do you ever hear such a night ? I be so frightened ! and Mary sleep so sound . " 

 Ruth be too much shake to be able to speak all at once ; but she take Elizabeth in her arm to reassure she . Elizabeth stand back . 

 " why , how wet you be , Mrs Denbigh ! and there be the window open , I do believe ! oh , how cold it be ! " say she , shiver .

 CHAPTER XXIV 

 the Meeting on the Sands 
 

 " he will take he away from I ! he will take the child from I ! "

Leonard would be take from she ! she have a firm conviction not the less firm because she know not on what it be base that a child , whether legitimate or not , belong of legal right to the father . and Leonard , of all child , be the prince and monarch . every man 's heart would long to call Leonard " child ! " she have be too strongly tax to have much power leave she to reason coolly and dispassionately , just then , even if she have be with any one who could furnish she with information from which to draw correct conclusion . the one think haunt her night and day " he will take my child away from I ! " in her dream she see Leonard borne away into some dim land , to which she could not follow . sometimes he sit in a swiftly - move carriage , at his father 's side , and smile on she as he pass by , as if go to promise pleasure . at another time he be struggle to return to she ; stretch out his little arm , and cry to she for the help she could not give . how she get through the day , she do not know ; her body move about and habitually act , but her spirit be with her child . she think often of writing and warn Mr Benson of Leonard 's danger ; but then she shrink from recur to circumstance , all mention of which have cease year ago ; the very recollection of which seem bury deep for ever . besides , she fear occasion discord or commotion in the quiet circle in which she live .  " in the middle of the damson , when they be just on the fire , there be a knock at the door . my brother be out , and Sally be wash up , and I be stir the preserve with my great apron and bib on ; so I bade Leonard come in from the garden and open the door . but I would have wash his face first , if I have know who it be ! it be Mr Bradshaw and the Mr Donne that they hope to send up to the House of Commons , as member of Parliament for Eccleston , and another gentleman , whose name I never hear . they have come canvass ; and when they find my brother be out , they ask Leonard if they could see I . the child say , ' yes ! if I could leave the damson ; ' and straightway come to call I , leave they stand in the passage . I bid he give it back to the gentleman , when they be all go away ; and I be quite surprised , and very uncomfortable , when Mr Donne say he have give it to Leonard , and that he be to keep it for his own .  CHAPTER XXV 

 Jemima make a Discovery 
 

 Mr Bradshaw have be successful in carry his point . his member have be return ; his proud opponent mortify . so the public think he ought to be well pleased ; but the public be disappoint to see that he do not show any of the gratification they suppose he to feel . 

 the truth be , that he have meet with so many small mortification during the progress of the election , that the pleasure which he would otherwise have feel in the final success of his scheme be much diminish . 

 he have more than tacitly sanction bribery ; and now that the excitement be over , he regret it ; not entirely from conscientious motif , though he be uneasy from a slight sense of wrong - doing ; but he be more pained , after all , to think that , in the eye of some of his townsman , his hitherto spotless character have receive a blemish . he , who have be so stern and severe a censor on the undue influence exercise by the opposite party in all precede election , could not expect to be spar by their adherent now , when there be rumour that the hand of the scrupulous Dissenters be not clean . before , it have be his boast that neither friend nor enemy could say one word against he ; now , he be constantly afraid of an indictment for bribery , and of be compel to appear before a Committee to swear to his own share in the business . 

 his uneasy , fearful consciousness make he strict and sterner than ever ; as if he would quench all wonder , slanderous talk about he in the town by a renew austerity of uprightness ; that the slack - principle Mr Bradshaw of one month of ferment and excitement might not be confound with the highly - conscientious and deeply - religious Mr Bradshaw , who go to chapel twice a day , and give a hundred pound a - piece to every charity in the town , as a sort of thank - offering that his end be gain .

" but as he end his speech he sigh ; and Mr Farquhar be none the less convinced that common report be true , which represent the clever , prosperous surgeon of Eccleston as bitterly disappointed at his failure of offspring .

Sally think that the mother ought to be tell ; what be dream send for but for warning ? but it be just like a pack of dissenter , who would not believe anything like other folk . Miss Benson be too much accustomed to Sally 's contempt for dissenter , as view from the pinnacle of the Establishment , to pay much attention to all this grumbling ; especially as Sally be willing to take as much trouble about Leonard as if she believe he be go to live , and that his recovery depend upon her care . Miss Benson 's great object be to keep she from have any confidential talk with Ruth ; as if any repetition of the dream could have deepen the conviction in Ruth 's mind that the child would die .

 CHAPTER XXIX

 the conversation narrate in the last chapter as take place between Mr Farquhar and Jemima , occur about a year after Ruth 's dismissal from her situation . that year , full of small event , and change of place to the Bradshaws , have be monotonous and long in its course to the other household . there have be no want of peace and tranquillity ; there have , perhaps , be more of they than in the precede year , when , though unacknowledge by any , all must have occasionally feel the oppression of the falsehood and a slight glance dread must have flash across their most prosperous state , lest , somehow or another , the mystery should be disclose . but now , as the shepherd - boy in John Bunyan sweetly sing , " he that be low need fear no fall .  CHAPTER XXX 

 the Forged Deed 
 

 Mr Wynne , the parish surgeon , be right . he could and do obtain employment for Ruth as a sick nurse . her home be with the Bensons ; every spare moment be give to Leonard and to they ; but she be at the call of all the invalid in the town . at first her work lie exclusively among the pauper . at first , too , there be a recoil from many circumstance , which impress upon she the most fully the physical suffering of those whom she tend . but she try to lose the sense of these or rather to lessen they , and make they take their appoint place in thinking of the individual themselves , as separate from their decaying frame ; and all along she have enough self - command to control herself from express any sign of repugnance . she allow herself no nervous haste of movement or touch that should hurt the feeling of the poor , most friendless creature , who ever lie a victim to disease . there be no rough get over of all the disagreeable and painful work of her employment . when it be a lessening of pain to have the touch careful and delicate , and the ministration perform with gradual skill , Ruth think of her charge , and not of herself . as she have foretell , she find a use for all her power . the poor patient themselves be unconsciously gratify and soothe by her harmony and refinement of manner , voice , and gesture . if this harmony and refinement have be merely superficial , it would not have have this balmy effect . that arise from its be the true expression of a kind , modest , and humble spirit . by degree her reputation as a nurse spread upwards , and many seek her good office who could well afford to pay for they . whatever remuneration be offer to she , she take it simply and without comment ; for she feel that it be not her to refuse ; that it be , in fact , owe to the Bensons for she and her child 's subsistence . she go wherever her service be first call for . if the poor bricklayer , who break both his leg in a fall from the scaffolding , send for she when she be disengage , she go and remain with he until he could spare she , let who would be the next claimant . from the happy and prosperous in all but health , she would occasionally beg off , when some one less happy and more friendless wish for she ;  her way be very quiet ; she never speak much . any one who have be oppress with the weight of a vital secret for year , and much more any one the character of whose life have be stamp by one event , and that produce sorrow and shame , be naturally reserve . and yet Ruth 's silence be not like reserve ; it be too gentle and tender for that . it have more the effect of a hush of all loud or disturbing emotion , and out of the deep calm the word that come forth have a beautiful power . she do not talk much about religion ; but those who notice she know that it be the unseen banner which she be follow . the low - breathe sentence which she speak into the ear of the sufferer and the dying carry they upwards to God . 

 she gradually become know and respect among the roughest boy of the rough populace of the town . they would make way for she when she pass along the street with more deference than they use to most ; for all know something of the tender care with which she have attend this or that sick person , and , besides , she be so often in connexion with death that something of the superstitious awe with which the dead be regard by those rough boy in the midst of their strong life , surround she . 

 she herself do not feel change . she feel just as faulty as far from be what she want to be , as ever . she well know how many of her good action be incomplete , and mar with evil . she do not feel much change from the early Ruth she could remember . everything seem to change but herself . " I do not know . it would be a great advantage in some respect ; and yet I doubt whether it would in other . his mother 's influence over he be thoroughly good , and I should fear that any thoughtless allusion to his peculiar position might touch the raw spot in his mind . "

 CHAPTER XXXIII 

 a mother to be proud of 
 

 old people tell of certain year when typhus fever sweep over the country like a pestilence ; year that bring back the remembrance of deep sorrow refuse to be comfort to many a household ; and which those whose beloved pass through the fiery time unscathed , shrink from recall : for great and tremulous be the anxiety miserable the constant watching for evil symptom ; and beyond the threshold of home a dense cloud of depression hang over society at large . it seem as if the alarm be proportionate to the previous light - heartedness of fancied security and indeed it be so ; for , since the day of King Belshazzar , the solemn decree of Doom have ever seem most terrible when they awe into silence the merry reveller of life . so it be this year to which I come in the progress of my story . 

 the summer have be unusually gorgeous . some have complain of the steam heat , but other have point to the lush vegetation , which be profuse and luxuriant . the early autumn be wet and cold , but people do not regard it , in contemplation of some proud rejoicing of the nation , which fill every newspaper and give food to every tongue . in Eccleston these rejoicing be great than in most place ; for , by the national triumph of arm , it be suppose that a new market for the staple manufacture of the place would be open ; and so the trade , which have for a year or two be languish , would now revive with redoubled vigour . besides these legitimate cause of good spirit , there be the rank excitement of a come election , in consequence of Mr Donne have accept a Government office , procure for he by one of his influential relation . this time , the Cranworths rouse themselves from their magnificent torpor of security in good season , and be go through a series of pompous and ponderous hospitality , in order to bring back the Eccleston voter to their allegiance .

 a portion of the Infirmary of the town be add to that already set apart for a fever - ward ; the smitten be carry thither at once , whenever it be possible , in order to prevent the spread of infection ; and on that lazar - house be concentrate all the medical skill and force of the place .

" it be but last night she keep my child quiet with sing psalm the night through . low and sweet , low and sweet , they tell I till many poor thing be hush , though they be out of their mind , and have not hear psalm this many a year .  CHAPTER XXXV 

 out of darkness into Light 
 

 the third night after this be to be the crisis the turning - point between Life and death . Mr Davis come again to pass it by the bedside of the sufferer . Ruth be there , constant and still , intent upon watch the symptom , and act accord to they , in obedience to Mr Davis 's direction . she have never leave the room . every sense have be strain in watch every power of thought or judgment have be keep on the full stretch . now that Mr Davis come and take her place , and that the room be quiet for the night , she become oppress with heaviness , which yet do not tend to sleep . she could not remember the present time , or where she be . all time of her early youth the day of her childhood be in her memory with a minuteness and fulness of detail which be miserable ; for all along she feel that she have no real grasp on the scene that be pass through her mind that , somehow , they be long go by , and go by for ever and yet she could not remember who she be now , nor where she be , and whether she have now any interest in life to take the place of those which she be conscious have pass away , although their remembrance fill her mind with painful acuteness . her head lie on her arm , and they rest on the table . every now and then she open her eye , and see the large room , handsomely furnish with article that be each one incongruous with the other , as if buy at sale . she see the flickering night - light she hear the ticking of the watch , and the two breathing , each go on at a separate rate one hurry , abruptly stop , and then pant violently , as if to make up for lose time ; and the other slow , steady , and regular , as if the breather be asleep ; but this supposition be contradict by an occasional repressed sound of yawning . the sky through the uncurtained window look dark and black would this night never have an end ? have the sun go down for ever , and would the world at last awaken to a general sense of everlasting night ?

 the end 
 

 a stupor of grief succeed to Leonard 's passionate cry . he become so much depressed , physically as well as mentally , before the end of the day , that Mr Davis be seriously alarmed for the consequence . he hail with gladness a proposal make by the Farquhars , that the boy should be remove to their house , and place under the fond care of his mother 's friend , who send her own child to abermouth the well to devote herself to Leonard .
